delicate

Suddenly, the world becomes so dark you can’t tell the difference between right or wrong anymore.

66:00 | violence is always the answer

A scream leaves the woman's lips when she's picked up by her hair, the gun in her hands being thrown to the ground. It hits the concrete, sliding away, and the other soul picks it up, a deep laugh leaving his lips as he cocks it himself, making sure it was loaded.

Not having any idea what was going on, Kim Soomi slowly opens her eyes. The red was gone in them, they were back to their normal state of green-blue, and it sparkles under the sunlight as she looks up.

Jungkook, Jinhwan, she knew they would be there to save her. After all, they'd been the one's who made up the plan initially, right? They were always her white knights when she needed them, never could she be more thankful.

Only until she saw neither of them standing before her, another laugh echoes through her ears. And it causes her vision to grow faint as she looks up fully, thinking she was hearing things.

"Oh, little sister, always getting into trouble somehow."

"Jaehyun?!" she cries, seeing the familiar, sleeked back dark hair, the same sharp jawline, and the same cocky smirk on his face when he saved her from something. The boy continues to chuckle as he steps forward, holding out a hand and grabbing her. She's pulled up before she could even understand what was happening, and Soomi has to hold onto her brother when she looks to who was still holding the psycho up by their hair, "S-Sunwoo?!"

Holding a hand to her head, it seemed like the world was spinning. There was no way this was happening right now, there was no way, it was impossible.

"How the hell are you guys here right now?!" she yells, unable to contain any of her overwhelming emotions as she tries to grasp this.

Her brother's finger is lingering over the trigger as he raises it, a playful grin on his lips when he holds it up to the woman Sunwoo was still holding. There was no doubt she was gonna have some bad hair loss, if she even lived after this. Frankly, Soomi wasn't sure what they were going to do, as Jaehyun only glances to her, "shouldn't we talk about that later? Let's start on why this crazy bitch thought it would be okay to fuck with my sister."

As soon as this angered statement leaves his lips, he steps forward to hold the gun to her head, leaning until he was directly in front of her face. "Well, ma'am, I haven't heard any explanation yet," he coos impatiently.

The lady only narrows her eyes, and at the sight of the dirty look he was giving Jaehyun, Sunwoo was tired of it. The Solar was standing right before him, and he couldn't embrace her yet because of this idiotic bitch. Not to mention, the fact anyone dared to threaten her life, he wasn't having it.

"I don't really care for one, honestly," he deadpans, and before anyone could stop him, he drops her to the ground. She's unable to reach when Sunwoo raises his foot, before slamming it against one of her wrists. Soomi winces at the crack that echoes through the ground, it was definitely fractured.

He does it to the other, and he only snorts when her screams echo through the air. It was a disgusting sight for anyone else to see, and although it had been a long time for her to see this sort of stuff, she was still used to it.

In a way, at least, until he'd picked her up by her hair again, humming, "oh darn, doesn't seem like you can fight back anymore with fractured wrists, you might want to get that checked out!"

The woman only yells and wails, begging for him to stop. But Sunwoo only chuckles as he holds out his hand for the gun, and Jaehyun didn't hesitate.

By this point, Soomi couldn't take it. She said she was used to this stuff still, but not to this extent. She'd seen them beat up many people, but never this bad, never this vulgarly.

Then again, this woman was about to pop a cap in her skull.

She buries her face in her hands when two gun shots echo through the air. Peeking through her fingers, she sees they'd gone into both of the woman's feet, making it where it would be agonizing if she ever wanted to walk. 

He was being tactical. It'd be stupid for him to kill her here, which was most likely what he was planning at this point. Sunwoo was always involved in bad things, with bad people, it was part of the reason their families never got along. His family wanted to work with hers, but they did so many illegal things that her father had denied it. In result, Sunwoo's family tried to steal his business, which created the entire war between them.

It was why they never wanted her to be with him, but the two had never cared. Their relationship was always strong no matter what people thought of them, and it was never supposed to change.

Poor Sunwoo never really knew what happened. He never knew the full story. All he was ever told by her siblings after Soomi's disappearance was that their parents disowned her because they found out about the drugs. The thing was, all of her siblings had been doing them as well. It was why it never made sense to him on why Soomi was the only one who was punished for it.

He was in the dark up until a few days ago, when called Jaehyun and told him about what he'd found online, about how he found Soomi. Only then, upon them speaking about her leaving, had he told him the full story. Suddenly, it had made sense to him why Chaerin and Juyeon got so iffy when asked about their sister, because it was their fault she left.

The woman's screams continue to echo through the air. "Who the fuck are you people? How does someone always save this slut?!" she's yelling in disbelief, but her words only earn her another gun shot in the leg.

"Call her something else, and it might be your head," Jaehyun's the one with the gun now, eyes burning from what she dared to say about his beloved sister, "I'll gladly make you my shooting range."

"You don't know her!" she continues to cry desperately, "you don't know what kind of things she's done, she's a fucking drug addict, stop protecting the guilty!"

The two boys exchange glances with each other, before bursting into fits of laughter. Sunwoo drops the helpless woman to the ground again, slamming his foot into her stomach and causing her to cough in agony, "sweetheart, we're all guilty here."

Through the tears in her eyes from the pain she was suffering, she looks up again at the faces of the two boys. It seems to wash over her, as she processes exactly what he meant, exactly who they were.

"You're all fucking disgusting," she hisses, "you people don't know what she's done, the amount of guys she's been with when she left-"

Gunshot.

Right in her stomach, causing the loudest scream of the night to leave her lips. Soomi was glad that no authorities or anyone could hear it thanks to the fact there was so much commotion from the arena. It was louder than physically possible for a human to scream.

Finally, she'd shut up after that, probably unconscious at this point.

Turning to Jaehyun, Sunwoo throws him the gun with a sigh, "Throw this bitch in the car, I know where we can take her," they both knew what he was referring to thanks to the sorts of people he was associated with.

But there was written confusion on her brother's face as he nods, before looking at what he was doing - walking away, "where are you going?"

Sunwoo wasn't walking away from them, he was just walking away from Jaehyun, and towards Soomi.

Noticing what he was doing then, the eldest brother shuts his mouth, shaking his head as a grin spreads over his lips. He bends down to pick up the unconscious girl, making his way to the car in a rush so he could chunk her in the back of the trunk before anyone had a chance to see.

"Sunwoo, I-" she starts, not even knowing what words she should say, what could she say? Where could she even begin?

"Solar," he breaths as if he'd just come up from water after drowning, as if he'd been drowning for years, for a decade. His arms wrap around her tiny, shaky body, and he pulls her forward until she hits his chest. "Fuck, I missed you."

She closes her eyes to intake the moment, her arms going under his leather jacket to wrap around his torso. Breathing deeply, she had to keep telling herself she wasn't dreaming, that this was really happening. She never thought she would see him again, or any of her siblings, but here they were, right in front of her. They saved her life, again, like they always had when she needed it most. 

Trying not to cry, she inhales the familiar scent of smoke and cologne. It was a pleasant mix she never minded from him, the boy who she dated for as long as she could remember.

Everyone always thought that Jungkook and Soomi's relationship had been long. They got together in around the end of 2014, dating up for the next few years until the scandal in the end of 2017. But Soomi had known Sunwoo since they were kids, and they'd practically gotten together in middle school.

She never thought about him when she left, she couldn't, it made her sad. And when she met Jungkook, she'd found a way to forget the boy she once adored by falling for another.

But here he was, and now she was in a complete tangle.

"I'm sorry," she blurts when they finally pull away, seeing Jaehyun was back from putting up the body now, "I'm sorry for disappearing like that, for never calling, never letting anyone know where I went," she pauses, trying to stop her eyes from tearing up and looking to her feet. Soomi was never one to cry, at least the Soomi that they knew. Back then, she was as strong as a rock because that was how she was raised to be. But now, crying was so common for her, but she didn't want to look weak in front of them.

"I was just so broken from what happened, when Chaerin and Juyeon blamed it all on me," she admits, blinking away her tears at the sky and forcing herself to go on, "I wasn't welcome in our house anymore, they told me I was a failure to the family, so I thought it'd be best if I just - left."

The two frown at the sight and her confession. 

"It's okay, little sis," Jaehyun says, wrapping his arm around her and pulling her into one of those big bear hugs he was always known for, "I'm sorry that I didn't do more, I should've told them the truth, that all of us were involved and not just you."

"It's okay, Jaehyunnie," she could only mutter into his chest, "it's okay."

"Mother and father realized their mistake," he blurts as their hug ends, and Soomi's eyes widen from his statement, "the house has never been the same, you can tell they're bitter and unhappy since the day you disappeared, and the fact that little Yein is growing up to look just like you has only made them resent her."

Her heart is a shattered mess on the floor when she hears this, she could only frown and shake her head, "oh my god."

"I don't spend a lot of time at the house anymore, I try to work long shifts so I don't have to," her brother wasn't done with the confession, though, as he goes on, "it's always constant screaming, always Yein crying, and she'll always ask me the same thing, when is big sissy coming home?"

Trying not to cry again, she couldn't help but ask, "what about Chae and Ju?"

Fixing his hair, he sighs as he looks to the sky. His same green eyes twinkle under the sunlight, and he thinks for a moment, "they miss you, they're usually just as bitter as mother and father, probably from the guilt," he hums, "Chaerin only yells when your name is mentioned, and Juyeon just locks himself up in his room."

Her mouth is open from the shock, "wow, I-I would've never have thought-"

"- Thought what, that we didn't miss you? Of course we do, Sol, every single fucking day."

Sunwoo's sudden snapping voice causes her to look back to him. His own brown eyes are glassy when they meet, and she lets out a shaky breath, "I'm sorry," she mutters again, "I'm sorry I hurt you guys."

"Stop apologizing," Jaehyun demands, nudging her shoulder gently, "and just come home, Sol."

She purses her lips from hearing his sudden offer. 

Come home, Sol.

Something she never thought she would hear, she'd heard so many things she would have never sought being true. To think she should've called out to Chaerin all those years ago, she should have talked to her. 

Even though she wanted to now, more than anything, she couldn't deny the life she had now. Looking down at her phone to check the time, she lets out a deep breath, "I-I can't now, I have a show," her eyes wander back to them, and she notices the pieces of paper in Sunwoo's pocket. Her eyes light up at the sight, "you guys bought tickets, didn't you? That's how you got here, so uh," she hesitates, a bit worried about what they would think about her music. But since they were here and they found her in the first place, it was clear they had heard it already. So, with a sigh, she grabs both of their hands and drags them towards the building, "come watch my stage!"



67:00 | resentment

"Where is she?!" he's crying frantically as he steps outside. The January air slaps the caramel boy across the face, and there were beads of sweat on his face still. When he and Jungkook came back from the producer's room, they just managed to sneak back before the actual KCON workers had been back to resume the show. With the show resuming, the next artist to perform had been iKON. Jinhwan didn't have a choice but to go on stage, but it was miserable performing when he knew she could be in danger. This psycho was no joke, there was no telling what she would try, and he knew poor Soomi wasn't that strong even when she acted like it.

Jungkook was just standing outside on the porch, and Jinhwan only grows frustrated when he holds out an arm, stopping him and preventing him from going any further.

Confused, he follows the maknae's gaze, landing on the girl. Soomi's brown hair was blowing in the wind, her green eyes glistening under the sunlight. There's a bright, wide smile on her face as she's hugging two guys he didn't know. The sight caused a pit to form at the bottom of his stomach, was she seeing other people that weren't him and Jungkook?

He didn't think Soomi was bad person for still loving Kook, he understood her situation. But would she really be with someone else as well? 

"Chill out," Jungkook says when he notices the bitter look on Jinhwan's face, "that's her brother."

"Her brother?" he repeats in surprise.

"Yeah," he hums, "but I don't know who the other guy is."



///




"Come on!" she's urging cheerily, dragging the two boys along with her whether they liked it or not. Her heels, that she'd put back on, click against the concrete, and she kept having to check the time every so often as they make their way towards the back entrance. Whether the security liked it or not, these two were coming in with her, and she would see to that.

"I can't believe Solar is seriously an idol," Jaehyun had been chuckling behind her with Sunwoo, "Sunwoo told me and I told him he was fucking crazy."

At the mention of her life now, she looks back to her ex boyfriend, raising a brow, "how did you find me, anyway?"

"Well," he clears his throat, looking a bit nervous to tell the story, "I ran into Yein at the ice cream parlor the other day, and she started telling me about the groups she watches," he begins, and Soomi's eyes widen as she listens to his story regarding her youngest sister, "so, she was saying how I should listen to this song called Only You, and I did when I got home."

Her breath hitches in her throat from what just came out of his mouth. Her little sister listened to her and Jinhwan's song? 

"I don't guess Yein ever recognized you, but the second I saw your face on the screen it hit me."

"Talk about a weird way to reunite," Jaehyun is muttering, scratching his head. A sigh leaves his lips, and he steps forward to walk by Soomi, wrapping an arm around her shoulders as he gushes, "but I'm proud of you, sis, you've really created something great."

She sends a thankful grin to her brother, "thanks, Jaehyunnie."

"Soo!"

It was a topic she had yet to talk about, her new name. Hearing it was odd to the two boys walking beside her, and they suspiciously look up at the sight of two new souls running at them.

Clearing her throat as they stop before her, their eyes going from her, to who she was with, she realized just what kind of situation she was in. 

"Jungkook, Jinan," she hums out nervously, "hi guys."

"Who was it?" Jungkook is the first to ask, "you caught them, right?"

She purses her lips in a thin line. This was the tricky part of the entire new situation that had been created. Her plan hadn't been to hurt the psycho, at least not as bad as her brother and ex had. Something like a weapon wasn't supposed to of been involved, she just wanted to send them to jail, although her anger had began to get the best of her back there. It happened to Jaehyun, too, she guessed it ran in the family.

Or maybe it was from their years of doing so many drugs.

Either way, she was dreading telling Jinhwan and the other boys of iKON. How would they react to hearing their own manager was behind all of this?

"Uh, yeah, I caught her," she admits, not meeting their eyes as she was worried they would notice how worried she was, "she's not gonna be a problem anymore."

Jinhwan is confused at her demeanor, "but who was it? Did you call the police?"

Sunwoo and Jaehyun were confused beside her. They didn't have any clue how deep this was, or how serious it had gotten. All they knew was that some woman was about to have blown Soomi's head off, and that was not okay where they were from. As far as either of them were concerned, she had it coming. 

But the two didn't know nor think that she had any relation to either of the random boys standing before them. Death was something that was taken lightly in the upper East side, at least in situations like this, it was no big deal.

"Are you talking about the lumpy bimbo that was trying to shoot my sister?" Jaehyun blurted, and Soomi grabs his arm, trying to signal for him to shut his mouth, but her older brother was always straightforward, "if either of you are concerned, I popped a few caps in her so she would shut her fucking mouth, she looked like some dark-haired jealous slut."

The two boy's faces grow pale from how casually he just said that. A humorous look takes over Sunwoo's face as he looks to them quizzically, "what, did you guys have something to do with her? I'd sure hope you don't being as she was about to hurt her."

Blinking, Jungkook's eyes go from Jaehyun to Sunwoo. He wasn't sure how he felt right then, he always tried to remain cool and collected, like nothing could bother him. But right now, he couldn't help but ask in confirmation, "I'm sorry, did you say - you shot her?"

An impatient sigh leaves Jaehyun's lips, and he's busy taking out a cigarette and a lighter as he mutters in response, "yeah, that's what I said. It's not okay for someone to threaten my little sister's life."

"What are you going to do with the body?"

"Oh, I've got someone I can take it to," Sunwoo hums, "if she's actually dead, that is, if not - they'll probably make use of her in some other way."

Soomi wrinkles her nose from realizing what he said. Slapping his shoulder, she groans, "can you not mention stuff like that? Talk about disturbing."

There's a playful grin on his lips, and he only wraps an arm around her shoulders, "sorry, princess."

Jungkook's mouth nearly fell open, and his eyes light up with anger. Jinhwan couldn't help but look up from the name that fell from his lips as well, having had been in deep thought about everything. They shot her, and he had noticed even after their stage, his manager was still nowhere to be seen. He tried and tried to think of some other way, but the coincidence seemed so right. Was the woman his manager?

"Sorry, but who the fuck are you?" Jungkook couldn't hold it in anymore when he blurts this out, his voice coming out a lot ruder than he intended. He couldn't hide the fact it bothered him that this guy was all over Soomi. It was bad enough he had to deal with Jimin for all those years, and now this Jinhwan guy. How many more could be added to the mix?

The boy wasn't even slightly intimidated by his tone, and that only annoyed Jungkook even more. When Soomi told him about her family and past life in New York, he didn't imagine them being like this. She always said they were rich and upper class, but they didn't seem that way, at least not from these two.

"I'm her ex boyfriend of seven years, and you?" Sunwoo smirks as he tauntingly asks, and both Jinhwan and Jungkook almost fainted.

Seven years. 

"What?" Jungkook blinks, looking to Soomi for any confirmation on this absurd statement, "is that true?!"

Holding a hand to her head, she wanted to sink into the ground as she sighs, "yeah, I dated him before I left to Korea."

The two newest love interests didn't know what to say. Too much was happening, and Jungkook rubs his temples as he replies to Sunwoo's previous question after receiving the answer from Soomi, "great, well I'm her ex fiance, nice to meet you."

For the first time, Sunwoo showed emotion as a bewildered expression took over his face. Jaehyun looked to him, and they exchanged the same shocked glance, trying to figure out if they just heard this kid correctly.

"Did you just say ex fi-"

"- Okay, well I have a stage to do, so why don't we all talk further afterwards?!" 





///





There's an uncomfortable silence at the dinner table. The only sound was the clinking of silver ware against plates and every so often chewing noise and sip of a drink. The now family of five sits at the table that seated seven, nobody looking at each other as they all only eat their dinner prepared for them.

Juyeon is silent, something that used to be very odd coming from him but had turned into the norm in the last five years. That same, playful boy was still somewhere inside of him, and he came out sometimes, but he was covered by a field of gray clouds that never seemed to go away. And poor Juyeon knew exactly what that field was; guilt.

Meanwhile, Chaerin had been trying to just peacefully eat her own food, but she could never seem to do that. The sound of that same stupid song Yein had been listening to for weeks now only continued to repeat itself and that same chorus, she wanted to slam her head into the table. Since she was sitting right next to her little sister, she could hear the song as if she was listening to it herself since the young girl had the volume so loud on her headphones.

"Where's Jaehyun?" mother had spoke up as she swallows a bite of her food.

None of the siblings look up. Juyeon was on his phone, Yein couldn't hear because of her music, and poor Chaerin just wanted to eat her food for once.

Noticing their mother's glare from lack of reply, the two siblings mutter almost in unison, "I don't know."

"Work," Chaerin offers with a shrug.

But their mother only furrows her brows, dabbing her face with the napkin in her lap before shaking her head, "he doesn't work on Friday's."

Still uninterested, Chaerin sighs, "then I don't know, mother."

Hoping that would be the end of it, her mother purses her lips before demanding, "call him."

Setting her fork down, it hits the plate with a clash. "Why do I have to?" she's complaining in annoyance, but her mother just gives her a look of annoyance. 

"Can you just please call your brother, Chaerin?" her father had spoke up, tired of hearing the girl always complaining. She'd been that way all her life, but ever since the disappearance, she'd been more negative than anyone could recall.

Heaving out a frustrated sigh, she pulls her phone out of her pocket. In their house, it wasn't appropriate to have your electronics at the table, at least that's what it was like back in the day. But now, all the children were using theirs, practically glued to them.

Holding the phone to her ear, she listens to it ring with a dull look on her face. The echo of that song kept repeating once again, and she balls her other fist that wasn't holding the phone at her side. It was hard for Chaerin to control herself, and feeling more upset than she could handle, she reaches up to rip the headphones off her little sister's head, "Yein, could you turn that down, please?!"

The little girl frowns from her big sister being mean to her. Not meeting her sister's flaming eyes, she grabs her headphones back, pausing the song she was listening to only momentarily. 

She wasn't surprised by her sister lashing out. The thing about Chaerin, was she did this often. Yein had learned to get used to it all, but it didn't mean she wouldn't cry about it. In fact, her sister and family being this way only made her cry more. 

Yein just didn't get it. She didn't get why they had to be like this, why didn't they look for her? All she ever wanted was to see her big sister again, her real big sister. Solar was never mean to Yein, she was the only one who would help her with her homework and play dolls with her. Without her, Yein was failing in school, and her mother kept yelling at her about it. But no one would ever help.

She could ask her biggest brother, but he was never home anymore.

Still not being done with her food, Yein doesn't say anything to Chaerin. She only silently puts her headphones back on, unpausing the song and trying to mind her own business.

Meanwhile, Chaerin was on the verge of breaking her phone from anger. Jaehyun never answered her calls, and it ticked her off. Her parents always asked her to do everything, and all the other siblings got off for free. Why was Jaehyun allowed to never be home but no one else could leave the house anymore?!

She wished she could go back to how it used to be, to being out every night with her siblings. Chaerin wished she could let go how she used to.

But now, she had no way to control her everlasting anger. 

"Turn it off already!" she cries, ripping the headphones off her sister's head again and throwing them across the room before Yein could take them back, "why the hell do you like that stupid song so much?!"

There are tears welling in her little sister's eyes when she looks to her. Their parents were heaving out deep sighs, and their father excuses himself from the table, not in the mood to listen to the siblings argue. As for mother, she knew it was helpless to do anything, but tried anyway as she calls, "Guys, let's not do this, please."

That song was still playing from Yein's headphones that laid on the floor, and it echoes through the room as silence overcomes the siblings. Realizing how she made her little sister feel, guilt begins to take over Chaerin's face. She couldn't help it, her anger controlled itself.

She opens her mouth to say something, but her little sister hugs the tablet to her chest that she watched the song on like it was her most prized possession. "I like this song," she sniffles, "because it reminds me of my big sister."

With that, she turns and picks up her headphones, putting them on her head again before running off upstairs. In her room, she makes sure to lock the door so nobody could bother her anymore. Yein had no wish to speak to anyone in her family anymore.

As tears stream down her face, she walks over to her bed. Grabbing a picture off her nightstand, she climbs on the pink duvet and crosses her legs, holding the photo while she stares at the picture. She could only peer down at the photo as she cries, listening to the same song over and over. Yein had yet to put her finger on it, but something about the girl's voice in her song always made her think of her big sister, it was why she couldn't stop listening to it.

And she never would, not until she found her again.


68:00 | the breakdown

"So, how exactly did you meet Soomi?" Jinhwan asks as casually as he could manage. The booming of the song that the girl was performing was heard loudly from all the speakers in the arena, and there were what felt like millions of screams as she sang the well-known song. It was astonishing for the two old friends to watch from someone like her. Never did they think when she left she would go in such a direction, but there she was, with a hundred people falling at her feet to praise her.

Although neither of them cared for this kind of music, there was no denying the talent that the small girl named Soomi, or should they say Solar, held.

Sunwoo had been staring at the girl from backstage, still trying to really piece it all together. Even though he was the one who found her thanks to Yein, it was so hard to grasp. His girlfriend of seven years, a girl he grew up, a girl stuck in the horrible chain of family drama in the upper East side. The way it always seemed to be was you didn't have a getaway if you were born into the richest family's of New York, you had to live through it and carry on whatever business they left to you, the family legacy, whether it was legal or not.

With the business profit only rising in a lively place like New York, it was often that the biggest family's went head to head. Everyone wanted to make the most money, get the most fame, have the state fall at their feet; but some family's wanted such so badly they tended to get dirty. It was exactly what Sunwoo was dragged into, and what he thought Solar would be drug into as well.

It seemed, in a way, she saved herself from having to deal with it. The entire drug scandal had almost been good as he watched her bright face now. But he still couldn't help but wish it hadn't happened. Just because everything was okay now, or would be, didn't mean he hadn't been broken for the last five years.

A sigh leaves his lips as he manages to tear his eyes away from her, looking back down to the really short guy he'd met. All he knew about him was he was the other guy in the song that Yein loved to listen to, being in some idol group he didn't care about. You wouldn't catch someone like Sunwoo listening to that genre of music, although he might get into Soomi's.

He was still in shock from hearing she was apparently engaged to the last guy, who had disappeared somewhere in the back. All he said was he had to get ready, before leaving, and no one really cared to ask anything else.

She was going to marry him, he scoffs, unable to help the jealousy that boiled inside of him, wonder what happened.

Even though he knew who Jungkook was since he introduced himself as her ex fiance, he was still completely clueless on this Jinhwan guy. He figured it was just a good friend of hers or something, so he didn't mind answering his question. 

"I grew up with her," he informs, eyes wandering back to the exact girl he was talking about, "our family's went head to head in the business world, and they were friends at one point in time, so we hung around a lot as kids," as he goes on, Jinhwan was listening intently. This guy, her ex boyfriend, and her older brother were insight to what her life had really been like. Hearing the fact they had killed whoever the woman was, who he still needed to ask Soomi about, wanting to know if he put the pieces together correctly, blew his mind more than words could explain. 

Never would he have guessed she would've dated a guy like this, or that her siblings would have been like this. They killed that woman in cold blood, but at the same time, Jinhwan didn't really blame them. Not that he had ever killed anyone or used a gun in the first place, but if she was really about to end Soomi's life, it had to be done. As far as he was concerned in the end, whoever it was deserved it for everything they caused.

The only worry was if they would be able to normally dispose of the body. If they did, would it really be safe wherever it was? Would they be able to keep the secret forever? 

"This fucktard had a crush on her for as long as I could remember," Jaehyun snorts from beside Sunwoo, who only shoots him a glare. Not bothered by it, he only giggles.

"Anyway," Sunwoo clears his throat in annoyance from her elder brother's words, before continuing with his story, "this massive fight broke out in our families, and we were forbidden to see each other, except as school. Solar and I always remained friends despite the rules, and we ended up doing a lot of dumb shit together."

He smiles from the nostalgia, his eyes twinkling under the backstage lights as he watches the girl move on the stage like it was what she was made to do, "We started dating around that time, my family was always about being dirty. "Jungkook..." her voice trails off as she stares down at the message. Her heart was on her sleeve, and tears well in her eyes as she kept rereading the things he said over and over.

Soomi's original plan had been to just not talk to her friends for the time being. She thought they were going to judge her, and not want to speak to her for a while so they could have time to really think about what they learned. Just because Junhoe had taken it so well when she told him, hadn't made her think everyone else would.

But they had, and seeing all their loving messages only made her realize that. She was getting through this, she was truly putting her life back together, with so many great friends at her side to help her do it.

Instead of running from her past, she thought, maybe she should have faced it from the beginning. 

However, if she'd done that, she would've missed out on so much.

So mayhaps, what was happening, now maybe this was the right path. Why should she care about the road not taken when this one seemed so glorious?

The car jolting forward from Sunwoo slamming on the break causes her to jump out of her thought bubbles. Her green eyes dare to wander to peer out the window, and she felt a pot of nostalgia pour inside of her at the sight. The old mansion, one Sunwoo had bought for himself so long ago, still looked the same. There were only a few differences to the outside, but it was exactly how she recalled it.

Thinking back to those times, no matter how hard they were, she couldn't deny how happy she had still been through out them. And knowing she was finally achieving real happiness once again, but this time the right way, only made it that much better.

Sunwoo had climbed out of the car a long time ago, which she hadn't noticed since she was too busy basking in her emotions. Her car door is opened, and he holds out a hand to her, peering down at her expectantly. 

Looking up to the boy, she's only thrown into more memories. Sunwoo really was her entire world at one point, much like Jungkook was at one point, too. Each of them, all three, had a special place in her heart that she couldn't deny. But Sunwoo was the only one who had experienced, been there, emerged, in the life that she once had. He knew what it was like because he was in the same boat as her all that time, he went through it with her by his side.

Because of that, because of the bond they formed since the day they met as children, was why she could never tear herself away from him now that he was back in front of her. Soomi wasn't saying she still loved him, because she didn't know what she used to feel for him in the first place. If it was love or not was foreign, but she did know that he'd always made her feel something no one else quite did.

It had been hard to leave, to live without him, when she did. She wondered how exactly he had lived without her, too.

In fact, if she wouldn't of met Jungkook, she might've came back for him.

"Sunwoo?" she blurts out his name in an inquisitive tone just as they're beginning to walk through the grass. He only looks back to her, stopping his movement to face her in wonder. 

"Uh - I wanted to ask about er - your life, you know, after I left," she stutters out, feeling weird asking him something like this.

He didn't seem bothered by the question. As they were already holding one hand, he grabs her other and grips them as if he was scared to let go. Brown eyes twinkling under the night sky that had taken over New York, he stares up above at the stars as he mutters, "lots of work, I was overcome by endless anger when I heard what your parents did to you," he begins, and she swallows the lump in her throat as she could only stare at his features as he spoke.

She really missed looking at him. Sunwoo had always been someone girls foamed at the mouth over ever since they were in middle school. With his defined jawline, pillow-like lips, and bright eyes, he was the ideal type of an casual girl - including her.

"I did job after job, and I killed people out of my anger at your parents for kicking you aside like that," he closes his eyes, as if he was trying to contain himself from getting upset about it even now, "and I was even mad at myself, for not doing something that night you left. Whether it was not letting you go, or just not giving you those fucking drugs in the first place. I blamed myself for everything, because it was my fault you ever touched drugs, making the underlying cause just that - me," she opens her mouth, but he doesn't let her speak as he only takes a short breathe before continuing, "I worried about you everyday, I missed you like hell. I'd go to your house every so often, thinking you might've come back, but no one would ever tell me anything. Chaerin and Juyeon changed, they were always so different, I figured it was because of them having to get off drugs."

"But in reality, it was the fact they didn't want to tell me the real reason you left, was because of them ratting you out instead of taking the fall with you," he scoffs, and he'd started to squeeze her hands out of anger. Remembering he'd hurt her, he calms himself again, "I'm still pissed at them, but I could tell they felt guilty, that they missed you, and what your brother said only proves that further."

Finally, he opens his eyes again, and they stare right into her soul. "So, there you go, Solar Kim, my life has been living hell since the day you left, and there hasn't been a millisecond you weren't on my mind."

She wondered if she could speak now as she only meets his gaze. Till he clears his throat, adding, "it makes me slightly upset you, on the other hand, were busy getting fucking engaged, but that's cool, Sol."

You could tell he wasn't thrilled about that news. She could only imagine his reaction when he heard the rest.

"I'm sorry," she pouts, "I didn't think anyone was having trouble without me, I thought you moved on."

He snorts as if she said something funny, "Solar, I was with you for seven fucking years, I didn't know what life was without you."

Guilt spreads over her like a wildfire. Her eyes avert to her feet, and Sunwoo notices the saddened look. Lifting her chin with a finger, he forces her to meet his eyes again. 

"Don't feel bad, though, okay?" he demands in a stern tone, "I'm not mad at you, you know I can't be, and you're back now," he's grinning again only a second later. His hand falls back to his side, and he lets go of her hand to wrap an arm around her shoulders, "and I hope you know, I'm not letting you go again."

"Kim Sunwoo~!" she's whining as he'd leaned so close to her ear his breathe was sending chills down her skin. Knowing it bothered her, he only giggles as she'd squirmed under his grip. Unable to get out of it since his arm was around her, she groans. Unable to help her temptation, she'd wrapped both of her small arms around his torso as she mumbles, "I missed you, Sunu."

The nickname was one he hadn't heard in years, and it was enough to play with his emotions as they walk onto the porch. He'd shoved the key in the keyhole of the lock so she couldn't see the big smile that spreads on his face.

If he was going to reply, he wasn't gonna get the chance to as the door clicks, signaling it was open. Pushing it open, he leans against it, motioning with one arm to the inside, "welcome home, Sol."

Entering the giant house, the brunette leans her head back. It was a wave of something she couldn't think of a word to describe, not euphoria but not exactly nostalgia either. She just felt ecstatic to be back in a place that brought her so much freedom in a time where she rarely ever had any. A place where she let herself go, found joy, and found herself.

The familiar scent of smoke didn't take long to enter her nostrils. Although she wasn't used to it anymore, it wouldn't take her long to be once again.

"Still the same, huh?" Sunwoo's voice hums from behind her in the dark. There wasn't a single light on in the house.

"Yeah."

A chuckle is heard from him, and she was confused as to why. It wasn't like she said anything funny. Sunwoo walks over to the wall, flicking the light switch, before the room was illuminated before her.

Soomi hadn't been expecting much. He wasn't someone who enjoyed things like interior decorating, so the only decor that had ever been in the house was something she put there. Since it had been so long, she assumed it would look exactly the same.

And it did, but that was the last thing she was focusing on when a dozen bodies jump up from hiding places in the room.

"Surprise, Solar!" they'd all screeched in unison, and the girl's face was of bewilderment.

She would've fainted if she didn't hit Sunwoo's chest when she took a couple steps back. He'd taken that as the chance to wrap his arms around her waist, a giddy smile on his lips as he leans his chin atop her head since he was so much taller than her. 

Her mouth was wide open like a hippo, and she covers it with her hands as she could only gawk at everyone standing before her, "oh my god."

Solar couldn't sleep.

Chanhee hums a song to himself as he flips the pancake on the skillet. His melodic, pretty voice flows through the air in sound waves, and if one were to hear it, they would probably assume the cute, pink haired boy was famous. In fact, it was shocking to know he wasn't. Really, Chanhee gave off an idol vibe, with the way he had his hair styled, the fancy clothes he wore, and how good he could sing. 

But a life like that wasn't one he could ever take. He and Solar always liked to sing together growing up. Ironically, they even joked a few times about being famous. Though neither of them ever imagined it was what they would actually do, at least he didn't. What happened with Sol and her family, though unfortunate at the time, had actually given her the opportunity to get out of the harsh reigns the castle had on her. Her parents kicking her out gave her the ability to actually pursue what she wanted to do, instead of being forced to go to business or law school to take on the family business.

He almost wished he could've had the same opportunity. But as the only child of the Choi family, there was no way he was ever getting out of something like this. His father's company was depending on him, and he was already attending Columbia University. This was what he had to do, no matter what he wanted.

Either way, Choi Chanhee was most definitely not someone to sit around and dwell on things. He was a vastly different person from his best friend, Solar, which was why he always had to remind her on what really mattered and keep her straight all the time. It seemed that without him, she'd been straying away from doing just that. It's okay, though, because she was back, and he wasn't intending to lose his best friend ever again. Even if she had to leave back to Korea soon, he would bother her to the ends of the Earth everyday.

It was early in the morning, and he wasn't surprised none of the others were awake. Always being a morning bird, he wasn't really phased by the fact he hadn't slept for more than four hours. Actually, Chanhee was used to it, he went to Columbia University, after all. Sleep wasn't in his forte. 

Humming along, he sets the last pancake onto the plate, that was piled high with over a dozen. He figured he needed to make a good amount if he was going to be feeding six people including himself. 

Satisfied with his creations, he claps his hands together triumphantly. Trailing across the kitchen floor of the mansion, he's about to fall onto one of the chairs at the breakfast table when the doorbell lets out a ding. It echoes through his ears, making them bleed from annoyance at the fact he was finally going to get a break.

Turning to the entryway that leads to the front door, he rubs his temples in frustration. It was probably the Fed-Ex delivering a package early or something, but he still wasn't thrilled about the interference. 

Flicking on the entryway light, he clicks the lock on the double doors. Pulling each handle open, the pink haired boy peers out into the morning world, not expecting to see who was actually standing on the other side of his front door.

Wind blowing through his hair and making it a mess atop his head, his leather jacket is hanging off one side of his shoulder, ear piercings dangling from his ears, and a intent look plastered on his face. Then again, Chanhee wasn't surprised as he peers at the boy standing on his porch, a blank look on his face as he sighs, "oh great, just the person I wanted to see at 10 in the morning."

Kim Sunwoo rolls his eyes, not caring much for the sarcasm Solar's best friend always sported. He wasn't here for him, anyway, so he cut straight to the point as he crosses his arms over his chest, deadpanning, "where's Solar? Let me talk to her."

No matter how intimidating most people found Sunwoo, Chanhee would never be one of them. Even though he could literally step on him if he wanted to, it didn't bother him in the slightest. He knew for a fact that Sunwoo could never actually lay a finger on him. Chanhee, after all, was Solar's beloved childhood, closest friend, if he ever hurt him, she'd hate him. 

Which was why he took it in his best interests to freely annoy the living fuck out of Sunwoo whenever he pleased.

"No," he hums blankly, "can't do that, pal."

Narrowing his eyes, he clearly wasn't pleased with the response he was given. "Are you fucking kidding me, is it really the time for this shit?" he snaps in bewilderment, impatiently, "I just need to talk to her about all of this, I'm not mad or anything, this is serious!"

Chanhee yawns from the fact Sunwoo wasn't impressing him and he was still tired. Leaning against the opened door, he shrugs, "she's not ready to see you, come back tomorrow."

Heaving out a deep exhale, Sunwoo's fists clench at his sides. His temper was always so bad, and it was clearly showing. It was taking all of him to not explode, as he closes his eyes momentarily to calm himself, before reopening them to look to Hee again.

"Chanhee," he breathes, "I know she's going through a lot right now, I know she's seeing her family today," he says calmly, "but please, I can't wait any longer, this is killing me. I just want to comfort her, don't you get that? None of it's her fault, I just want her to know she should've told me, that it's okay."

His abruptly heartfelt words took Chanhee back for a second. The shock is shown on his face, and he raises a brow from surprise as he takes in what he just heard from the cold-hearted gang leader.

For once, Sunwoo was looking at him pleadingly. Honestly, it was sort of scary. So much, that he finally groans, "alright, but just stay in here, I'm going to talk to her first," he commands, pointing a finger at him as if he could ever be terrifying. Sunwoo chuckles at the attempt nonetheless, gladly taking the invitation as he steps into the Choi mansion.

"I won't move," he assures him as they walk into the living room.

Already walking to the stairs, Chanhee takes a few steps before he turns back to Sunwoo, "you're really still that fucking whipped for her, aren't you?" he snorts, a knowing look on his face that told Sunwoo he didn't need to even reply. Giggling from the fact he knew it too well, he spins on his heel, "oh dear, this is one big mess," he mutters as he begins up the steps to talk to the girl.

He didn't think Sunwoo heard him, but he had. And he knew that he was no doubt right about that.

Jungkook felt like he was dying.

A sigh leaves his lips, and he dully leans back into the mattress of his hotel bed. His body sinks into the plush, and he lets his head be buried by the soft pillow as his brown irises blankly stare up at the boring ceiling.

He had a point. 

"Yeah," he sighs, "yeah, you're right."

Nodding, he leans down to take another bite of the burger. Chewing, Jungkook swallowed the food before he heaved out a sigh, "I just miss her," he admits, "I know she's busy with her family life now, but I can't help but miss her."

He thought Jimin was going to call him selfish, or even stupid. But when he looks to his friend, he was only peering at him em-pathetically. 

"Me too, Jungkook," he mutters, "me too."

But she knew this had to happen, as afraid as she was, she couldn't postpone it forever.

"Jinhwan's stage should be over by now," he whispers, his lips just above her ear as his chin was gently atop her head. 

She pursed her lips upon hearing him say this. Jinhwan, she forgot he still had to do the main stage with iKON, that was where he had been all this time, preparing for it. 

"Are you gonna be okay?" she felt the need to ask, even though she probably knew the answer.

She also knew Jungkook probably wasn't going to tell her the truth. "Yeah, Mi, I'll be okay."

Soomi only sighs, not knowing what else to say. She still had a long day ahead of her, as she sat there in his arms. Jungkook really had been her happiness at one point in time. He really had saved her from the horror she felt, how alone she felt when she came to Korea all alone, pursuing what seemed like a silly dream to everyone else. From the first day at Big Hit, he believed in her. Through out the time they trained together, he taught her how to have confidence in who she was. That was how he saved her, and it was what made her love him.

But perhaps the love she had for him, was a different type of love she didn't understand. She adored Jungkook because he pulled her out of a dark place, he was a reliable friend to her whenever she needed one. However, he'd destroyed her at the same time, he ruined her, trashed everything she once thought she knew. For a year, she was left without understanding, not knowing what she did wrong. She was left all alone as her life seemed to crumble before her.

Then she met Jinhwan. From the first time they made eye contact in that elevator, all he ever did was help her. Even though they had fought before, he always saw his wrongs, he admitted to them, and he grew into a better person. Never had he done her wrong, never had he made her feel less, all he'd ever done was praise her, make her feel like she belonged here - like she belonged with him.

Which was it, that was the only place she ever felt she belonged. When she was with him, everything felt right, like the world had finally fallen into place. Although she found happiness in Jungkook, she found love in Jinhwan, she found euphoria, she found who she was meant to be with.

Despite everything wrong she had done in her life, Jinhwan loved her for it all. He didn't get mad if she did something, he accepted it, he saw her side, and he helped her through it. He was selfless but selfish when he needed to be. No matter what, he always seemed to say the right thing. He'd found out all of her darkest secrets that she was always so afraid to tell a soul because the fear of being judged, but they only made him love her more, not the opposite.

"Soomi?" her heart explodes with joy at the sound of such a voice.

Jungkook dully watches the way he explained, the way her green eyes would brighten. Slowly, he let her leave his arms, he let her go to him, even as much as it hurt him to do so.

"Jinhwan," she gasps out, as if she had just come up out of the water for air. Her feet slam against the concrete, bringing her right to him. The caramel boy is shocked when she wraps her arms around his torso, burying her face in his chest and clinging onto him for dear life. He'd never felt her hug him so tightly, so meaningful, and it caused him to send a confused look Jungkook's way, trying to gather what was going on.

He was still a sweaty mess from his stage, but even then Soomi didn't care. The feeling of him enclosing his arms around her, squeezing her gently back as a sign of affection, made her want to scream - not out of anger, but just because she was so happy. She was absolutely ecstatic whenever she looked at him, whenever she saw him, and she finally wasn't afraid to say that.

Jungkook's doe eyes meet his, and he only sent him a close-lipped, bitter smile. The sight only had Jinhwan feeling more lost. What was up with that? Jungkook hated Jinhwan, so why would he ever look at him like that - like he lost?

With that, Jungkook bowed politely, before spinning on his heel, and walking away. Jinhwan watched him leave with the most blank look on his face. He hadn't heard the song Jungkook wrote because he'd been preparing for his own stage and getting ready in the guys' dressing room. So, he was completely clueless as to what could be going on that day.

Still beyond confused and curious of the answer, he looks down to the girl that was squeezing him to death. "Soo, I was looking for you, you missed my stage," he hums, running his fingers through her hair as she only continued to further snuggle herself into his chest, "I tried extra hard for you, too, I even did those adlibs you always complain about me skipping," he giggles lightly, referring to how she always bothered him about such, "but it's okay, I can see that you must've been busy. Do you want to talk about it?"

There it was, one of the reasons she adored him so dearly, in a different way than she saw Jungkook or Sunwoo. A way she could only explain with three words, three words she had never meant so intensely. 

"Nani," she's breathless as she pulls away from the hug. Jinhwan looks down at her with curiosity, and his eyes widen when he sees the tears in her eyes. His hands reach up, and he uses his thumbs as he cups her cheeks to wipe them away. Before he opened his mouth to speak, most likely about why she would be crying and what was going on, she blurts out, "I love you."

Since it was something they were used to saying to each other, he didn't understand. "I love you, Soomi, but why are you crying?" he pouts, continuing to wipe the tears away.

She laughs, she laughs loudly and obnoxiously, probably loud enough for people inside to hear. Through her tears, she laughed like she never had before, like this was the funniest thing ever. "I'm crying because I'm happy," she admits, placing her hands atop his that were still cupping her cheeks, "I'm happy just being right here, with you, happier than I've ever been in my life."

Jinhwan was peering down at her like she was crazy, but it was something he loved about her. He grins like a kid, nodding slowly as he tries to understand what she was getting at. Knowing he still wasn't aware of what she meant, she continues to giggle away. 

"You're cute," he states, "and I'm happy that you're happy, but what was with Jungkook looking like a zombie?"

"Nani," Soomi sighs dramatically, poking his nose with her pointer finger and shaking her head, "you still don't get it, do you?"

Raising a brow, he shrugs, "Soo, I'm not sure what it is I'm supposed to be getting."

"You," she practically yells in exasperation. When he only continues to stare down at her in contemplation, she chuckles, lowering her voice to a mere whisper as she informs breathlessly, "I choose you."


97:00 | a new friend

Jinhwan and Soomi couldn't exactly cling onto each other the way they wanted to since they were still backstage at KCON. Despite this, it was still obvious the brunette was a jumpy, giddy mess as she practically ran back inside with him behind her. Jinhwan kept giggling away at her cute actions, clearly thrilled himself with what just happened.

It was over, he still couldn't comprehend it, Soomi was his. After all this time, he got to be with the girl he loved. He'd never felt such an explosion of emotions in his life. His veins were pumping faster than ever, with only endless adoration for her, his girlfriend. Could he really call her that now? It didn't seem real.

In fact, he was so happy, he didn't even think about what Soomi was going to do about her other ex boyfriend. Little did he know, she was going to see him later.

There's plenty of chatter going on in the backstage area. Now that everyone was done with their stages, they could check in with their staff and head back to wherever they wanted. Soomi jogs to where her family and old friends were, only to see the other boys of iKON were there too.

As soon as she joins the group, Chanhee's eyes immediately fall on her. Stepping closer to her, he crosses his arms over his chest as he sighs, "Solar, dear, your new best friend is making my brain bleed."

Raising a brow at him, she really didn't expect anything less. "I'm seriously offended you replaced me with that," Hee goes on with a disappointed sigh, "it's not even funny, how would that ever assist you with anything?" he motions to Junhoe, who was currently dancing around with Yein. The girl was in fits of laughter as she watched him, who was waving his arms around in a wiggly manner.

Sighing, she holds a hand to her head. This was going to happen sooner or later. "Hee, we already went over this," she shakes her head, "also, he's not even who I went to for advice and stuff, you haven't met Jimin."

"Jimin?" he hums, "where might I find him?" he turns to look around at the crowds of people, expecting this Jimin to pop out of nowhere.

Solar groans, tired of her bestest friend doing things like this. He had always done this, from her friends to her boyfriends. Although he was just looking out for her in a way, he was also the definition of petty.

"Are you bothering Sol again about her newer friends?" Jacob sighs as he walks up to the two, followed by Kevin and Changmin.

"dude, get over it that you're not the only best friend she has," Changmin pouts, "she's always had us too, you know!"

Hee rolls his eyes, "sure, but you've never been as high on the spectrum as me."

Seeing the offended look that takes over their faces, Solar clears her throat, knowing she should interfere now. "Can you guys cut it out? This is idiotic," she exhales deeply, "we aren't ten anymore."

Figuring it was over, she was glad she could finally tell them what happened. Before she even got a chance to open her mouth, giddily about to share with her friends that she was now taken, Kevin had practically screamed so high-pitched it made all of their ears ache. The four turn to him in awe and frustration, about to ask what his problem was, but he beat them to it with the explanation, "Holy shit, look!"

Just hearing him say that, they all knew what it was. Annoyed sighs leave everyone's lips except Solar's, as she could only peer at the figures Kevin was pointing to. She had obviously seen them before, and she knew who they were. However, she had never spoken more than a mere greeting to any of them.

"Talk about being fucking ten," Chanhee mutters.

"It's NCT, it's them!" Kevin ignored his other friends comment, turning to the famous one out of them all, he clung onto her arm as he begged, "Sol, you have to introduce me, please - I'll do anything!"

"Kev," she whines, "I don't even know them!"

"But don't you talk to each other since you're both famous idols or whatever?!"

"It does not work like that!"

"Just leave her alone, idiot, she doesn't want to be apart of your childish antics," Chanhee snaps, punching the boy's shoulder, "if you're so desperate, go introduce yourself."

Kevin pouted like a child who had been denied candy. Solar groans as she thought about his request, but she seriously didn't want to randomly walk over there and start talking to a bunch of guys she didn't really know. She just became official with Jinhwan, how would that make him feel?

Speaking of, she realized, looking around in confusion, where was he?

"Guys," she clears her throat, glancing to her friends, "I'll be back."

Her friends hum in understanding, and she pushes past them to walk over to the other six boys of iKON that had been talking to her family. They were all rather occupied, so she taps on one who seemed the least involved in the conversation.

"Bob, do you know where Jinhwan went?"

He pursed his lips, thinking about it for a second. "Probably to change out of his stage clothes and check in with our new management team so we can leave," he informs with a nice smile.

"Ah, okay," she nods, and before he might ask another question, Solar spun on her heel, and jogged away.

Letting out a sigh, her heels click against the concrete flooring as she walks. She was glad she finally got a hang of finding dressing rooms at this point.

Pulling her phone out of her pocket, she checks for any messages from him. She guessed he didn't really feel it was necessary to text her about something like that. But was she also expecting a text from someone else?

She couldn't lie, she was worried about Jungkook. All she could do was believe that everything he said, he meant it. But even then, knowing he was hurting because of her made her feel horrible.

Not to mention, the other boy she would be seeing tonight. Should she tell Jinhwan about it? She knew they agreed not to keep secrets, but she didn't want to stir up anything. They just got together, it was what they'd both been waiting for this entire time, it just took Soomi longer to realize it.

It wasn't that she still had feelings for Sunwoo anymore. They hadn't been together since she was seventeen. Everything she did with him was in the past, and she was not planning to relive it anytime soon. In fact, the entire reason she was meeting up with him was to tell him that. The thing that worried her was just him, Sunwoo. There was no telling what he would try, but it would probably be something. Solar wasn't trying to cheat on the first day of her being with someone.

Groaning, she shoves her phone back in her pocket. "It'll be fine," she assures herself aloud, not caring if anyone heard her and thought she was weird, "you'll get through this, just resist whatever he tries to do."

She'd been giving herself such a confident pep talk, that she nearly screeched when she suddenly heard something she hadn't expected. A laugh, there was someone laughing, brightly and loudly, all in a giggle that sounded undeniably precious. It was a type of laugh she had never heard before, causing her to glance up at the direction it came from.

That was when she realized they had been laughing at her.

The boy's honey brown eyes meet hers, noticing she saw him giggling at her. Still, he didn't appear distressed about it as she stops, only sending a smile her way, "ah, sorry," he hums, "I just admired the pep-talk you were giving yourself."

Solar frowns, not believing a word this stranger was saying to her, "yeah, right, you were making fun of me."

He pouts a little, "hm, no, I wouldn't do that," shaking his head vigorously. There was a certain brilliance when he smiled again, and Solar cleared her throat, diverting her eyes from the brightened face of this new presence.

He was clearly an artist, why else would he be here? She swore she knew who he was, but for some reason her mind seemed to be messing with her. Why couldn't she think of his name or what group he belonged to? She was usually good with stuff like that because she tended to know everyone.

Solar is snapped out of her trance of deep contemplation by the sudden close proximity between her and the new soul. His eyes are sparkling when they look down at her, he was tall. Not as tall as Junhoe, but taller than Jinhwan, she had to look up directly to meet those eyes. Finally, he cleared his throat, "we've met before, but I don't think you remember me," he explains, but didn't sound offended at all, "Haechan."

Haechan as in full sun? She had to hold in her giggle, what a cute name. 

Glancing down, she noticed he was holding out his hand to shake her own. Pursing her lips, she accepts the exchange. His palm was warm under her own, and her hand burned when it fell back to her side. Only then did she manage to speak out her name, "Soomi - and uh - I'm sorry, I don't remember us meeting before, I have a sucky memory."

He shrugs it off, not appearing a have a worry in the world, "don't worry about it, it happens. I think you know my members though, I'm from NCT."

Oh right, she tried not to gawk, clearing her throat, Kevin would be crying right about now.

Thinking about her poor friend's obsession with them gave her an idea. Maybe it would be convenient for her to make friends with one of them, then she could make little Kevin's dreams come true.

"Ah," she nods, "you guys have that one song that always gets stuck in my head - Regular!"

Giggling, he grins from ear to ear, "yeah, that's ours!"

"I always liked that one 'I'm so clean, so fresh,' part."

"Really?" he beams, "I'm thrilled to inform you that's my part."

"Funny," she hums, before Haechan spoke up about how he really liked her music, too. 

The next ten minutes you'd find them just laughing away. Believe it or not, he was a crazy nice person with a very interesting sense of humor. If she was to compare it to anyone, she'd probably say Junhoe, whom she really could not stand sometimes but at the end of the day, he was her best friend. With this in mind, Soomi felt like she and Haechan could be great friends.

She also figured Kevin would be very pleased to her this news.

A rapid dinging of incoming text messages began in her pocket. Solar wouldn't of noticed them if she hadn't heard rapid footsteps coming down the hallway, and a screeching little voice that ripped her from the conversation she was having.

"Sissy, sissy!"

"Yein!" she gasps as the child ran up to her, immediately grabbing her hand and clinging onto it like her life depended on it, "Hey, why would you run back here yourself?! That's dangerous."

But the little girl only shrugs, "Bobby said you would be back here and that if I couldn't find you I should just scream."

Solar sighs in disappointment, "sounds like something he'd say."

Yein nods, a grin on her adorable face, before she slowly turned to notice the stranger. Blinking a few times, she narrows her eyes in concentration, seeming to look over every detail of the boy. Solar was going to introduce them since she was here in front of him, but she didn't get a chance to when her sister pointed a finger at him, "wait, it's the guy from the group Kev likes, sissy - eNsitea!"

Her pronunciation made Sol sigh and Haechan burst into fits of giggles. Haechan gushes as he bends onto his knees to reach eye level with the kid, "hi, I'm Haechan, I'm friends with Soomi."

"Hi, I'm Yein!" she waves brightly, but couldn't help but look up to her sister in confusion, "you told Kev you weren't friends with any of them."

"Well, I wasn't," Solar scratches the back of her head awkwardly, "until approximately twenty minutes ago."

Yein pursed her lips as she turns back to the boy. Her same green eyes peer at him in focus, and no one knew what she was thinking. Until she blurts, "sissy, he's cute," before looking to him again, "do you think my sissy is cute?"

"Um," he chuckles, unsure of what to do, "sure."

"Oh my God," Solar could only groan in disappointment at her little sister, "Yein, cut it out, I just met him like three seconds ago, and you know it's not okay to do that," she sternly lectures her playful baby sibling.

Pouting, she thought for a moment before her mouth formed an o, "uh oh, I forgot, you're with Jinawn, I hope he's not mad at me!" Her eyes pool with worry, and before you knew it, she was pulling on her sister's arm. Apparently, Yein had no idea that Jinhwan wouldn't have any idea about what happened since he wasn't here to witness it. Solar guessed her sister just had a big heart, as she cried out, "come on, sissy, take me to Jinawn so I can apologize!"

"Yein, you don't have to apologize," she told her sister, not really wanting to bring this up to her boyfriend. Exhaling, her sister only continued to try to pull her down the hall. Turning to Haechan, who was just patiently standing there, she offers him an apologetic smile, "it was nice to meet you, Haechan, sorry about my little sister - she's different."

"Don't worry, she's cute," he waves a hand of dismissal, "but it was nice to meet you too, again - I'll see you around, Soomi."

She nods, before shortly waving as she finally let Yein pull her away. Haechan chuckles as he watches them leave, shaking his head in awe. He could hear Solar sighing in exhaustion as she informed her sister, "you don't even know where the room is, why are you dragging me?!"

Inhaling, he spins on his heel away from the scene to continue where he was going in the first place. The others had probably texted him a million times about where he was, but they probably got distracted messing around backstage that they forgot to come find him. It was what usually happened, anyway.

The entire walk back to his friends, he found himself wondering what it was Yein had been talking about. Soomi, the biggest solo artist, was dating someone? He pondered in confusion, but wasn't that prohibited?

Pushing it to the back of his mind, he tried to shrug it off, even though the name she had uttered was stuck in his mind. It wasn't his business, anyway. 


98:00 | sister talks

"Jinawn!" Yein had been screeching as she ran into the dressing room, far ahead of poor Soomi who had tried telling her little sister to not bring up what just happened. She should've known Yein wasn't going to listen, and sure enough, there she went. "Jinawn, I'm sorry, I hope you can forgive me!"

Jinhwan had appeared to of just changed out of his stage clothes. A red hoodie loosely hung on his body, and a pair of skinny jeans hugged his legs. He was staring at his reflection in the mirror, fixing his caramel hair as he slid a beanie over his head. Soomi's breathe hitched in her throat when she saw him turn around, brown eyes twinkling when he saw who'd entered the room. There's a welcoming grin on his lips, only until he heard the words Yein said. 

Confused, he furrows his brows as he looks to her older sister for context. Solar sighed as she met his eyes, shaking her head as if to tell him not to listen to her. Jinhwan purses his lips as Yein had wrapped her arms around his waist, hugging the life out of him with her tiny arms. 

"What is it, Yein?" he hums, "You know I've never be mad at you."

Her green eyes widen as she pulls away from the hug. Jinhwan had been grinning at her from how cute she was, but when those certain words came out of her mouth, his smile faltered. 

"Uh," he blinks, not understanding, as he looks up to his girlfriend, "who's Haechan?"

"Yein," Solar snaps in a stern tone, and her sister frowns as she looks to her, "didn't I tell you to cut it out?"

When Jinhwan's blank expression didn't change for a while, she began to grow a bit worried. It hadn't even been a day yet of them being officially together, was it already ruined? She was not looking to have her first fight on day one of her relationship with Jinhwan. Soomi had waited way too long for this.

Her heart was dropping, until that smile spreads over his lips. Shaking his head, his sneakers click against the tiled floor as she walks up to her. Soomi inhales his cologne in relief when he wraps his arms around her, she thought she was about to die. 

"Silly, you don't have to tell me that," he shakes his head with a chuckle, resting his chin atop her own, "what Yein said made me think he was flirting with you, I thought I was going to have to go find him."

"No," she whines, wrapping her own frail arms around his torso and burying her face in his hoodie, "it wasn't like that at all."

"Good, because now you're finally mine, and I won't tolerate any of that," he gushes, pulling away so he could kiss her forehead. Soomi's cheeks had burned with rose as she could only look up at him in awe, she shouldn't of taken so long to make this decision. It annoyed her that it had been clear for so long, but she was too stupid to figure it out. 

Although, she'd always love Jungkook, too. But it was different from the love she had for Jinhwan.

"Anyway, did you hear? Your parents invited me and the guys over for dinner," he shared brightly, grabbing her hand and intertwining their fingers, "I don't know what time it is, but we should probably get going. I think they already left by now to prepare it."

Soomi giggles, "oh, they must really like you guys," she cleared her throat, feeling the need to correct him on something, "but my parents don't do the cooking - they usually have staff for that."

Jinhwan raises his brows in surprise, "right, I forgot you're that rich."

Rolling her eyes, she nudges his side, but he only laughed at her. Jinhwan looked to the child that was on the couch, "Yein, are you ready to go?"

At the sound of her name, the girl pipes up in excitement, practically scrambling off the couch, "yeah, I'm hungry, and I want to see Joonhay again!"

Solar bursts into fits of laughter from how she said his name, as if Jinawn wasn't enough. "God, I really need to teach you pronunciation."

Jinhwan only shakes his head in awe, holding out his other hand for Yein. The girl grabs it instantly, looking like the happiest child in the world. Seeing her poor little sister so bright made Solar feel good. Happiness was what Yein deserved, and she was finally getting that. 

She wouldn't want it any other way. She was thankful for the decision she had made, but it took a lot of help for her to do it.

She had plenty of people to thank for it.

"let's go."

Groaning, she sets her phone down, not wanting to look at it anymore because it would onloy continue to tempt her. She hadn't actually tried to text Jungkook herself, hence why she went to Jimin first because she just wanted to know how he was doing. It was true, he most likely needed a while away from her whether he would admit it or not. Just the fact she knew he was hurting, though, was really messing with her head.

A deep exhale leaves her lips as she turns back to her face in the mirror. Her green irises peer back at her, but yet she couldn't truly decipher the emotion within them. What was she feeling right now? Soomi was pretty sure she was happy, she should be. Jinhwan and her were finally together, and they were having dinner with her family whom she never thought she would be able to face again. The stalker that ruined her life for months was gone, and though there might be another one on the lose, there was no proof of such. For once, she almost had nothing to worry about.

Except for Sunwoo and Jungkook.

Groaning, she shakes the thought away as she checks the clock on the bathroom wall. She had yet to eat dinner as it was only 7 PM, she still had a while until she had to go to the castle park to meet him.

Trying not to think about it, she realized she should probably get downstairs to see what was going on. Jinhwan and the others were probably confused as to what was taking her so long. 

Just as she fixes her hair and makes sure her makeup isn't tainted, a knock sounds from the door. "Sol, are you alright?" her sister's voice breaks through her mind, and she purses her lips as she heard what she asked.

She could talk to Chaerin about all this, couldn't she?

"Chae," she sighs as she clicks the lock on the door, pulling it open to reveal her sister's concerned face, "do we have a while till dinner?"

Not expecting the question, her sister thinks for a second. "Probably, I just came to check on you because your boyfriend seemed like he was on the verge of death without your presence," she snorts, "he's real attached to you, what do you even do to get guys like this?"

Solar rolls her eyes, reaching out and grabbing her sister's wrist. Pulling her into the bathroom, she closes the door and turns to her shocked expression. "I need to talk to you."

Blinking at her a few times, Chaerin nods slowly, "Oh, okay, what is it?"

The two sisters used to have heart-to-hearts rather often. This was something they were used to, even despite all the fights they used to have when their relationship got rocky. In the end, they knew they could always come to each other for serious things. It was what sisters were for.

Running a hand through her hair out of stress, she sighs, leaning against the locked door, "this whole thing, me and Jinhwan just became official today, you know. I broke my ex-fiance's heart who a part of me still loves, and I have to go meet up with Sunwoo at 11 in the park to break the news to him, too," she vents to her intently listening younger sibling. "I don't know how he's going to react to all this, and to make it worse, I have to go back to Korea within the next couple of days."

Her eyes widen at the last sentence, "really? You're going back this early?"

Scratching the back of her head, she pouts guiltily, "Yeah, I'm not sure if I have a choice otherwise."

Breathing out in a dull manner, her sister shakes her head, "Jeez, Sol, you've always had such a package of problems with you."

"I know."

"Maybe if you'd stop doing whatever it is you do that makes every guy want you, you know," Chaerin scoffs playfully, and Solar only wrinkles her nose in response. "I think it might not of been the best idea for you to get into a relationship right now, sounds to me like you've still got a mighty crazy attachment to Jungkook."

"But I love Jinhwan," she insists, "it's just - with Jungkook it's different."

Chaerin stares at her blankly for a second, before she deadpans, "you're really fucking complicated."

It's a scary thought, a scary thought that everything you once knew is about to change. The life you were so accustomed to over the last half a decade was changing. It's a scary thought, that turns into a horrifying one, but after you think about it long enough, it almost becomes comforting.

She was getting a break from being on the run, in constant fear from someone who tried to kill her. It was terrible for her to be in contact with him not only because it was risking her career, but it was also risking her relationship. All around, it was dangerous for her.

It had to be done.
