With the worry of not only that, but her stalker, weighing her down — Solar did the only thing she knew to do anymore.

She turned to her old friend, and she didn't mean Chanhee.

"Sweetheart, as much as I love you, you know I can't be giving you so many for free, right?" The gang leader raises a brow at the desperate girl, peering down at her with those dark eyes of his, "it puts a dent in our inventory, you've been sucking these pills down like fucking snacks."

She's unimpressed. Crossing her arms over her chest, the brunette rolls her eyes, "but you guys are rich and always get more, right?"

As hard as it was to say no to her, Sunwoo was still unsure. Thankfully, a presence suddenly appeared beside her. "Sol, you're going to overdose if you keep taking them like you are," Sangyeon advises her, placing a friendly hand on her shoulder, "you might want to cut back for at least twelve hours."

Cursing the boy mentally for being there at that time, she sighs as she turns to him, "I don't want to say you're wrong because I know you're right but — I just really need them."

Sangyeon glances from Sunwoo to her, worry filling his irises, "Sunwoo, how much did you give her? Look at her pupils, they're so dilated she looks dead."

The crime boss blinks a few times in thought, "do you think I was keeping count? I didn't think she would ask for as many as she probably has," despite his lifeless tone, you could tell he was feeling some remorse, "which is stupid of me — Solar, I've gotta cut you off for a while."

She gawks at his sudden change of mind, "huh, that's not fucking fair!"

"Chill out, princess," he groans, "you're having some serious cravings after not doing them for so long, I'm not going to let you fucking kill yourself."

Before she could say anything, he holds out a cigarette to her, "but if it helps, take this instead. It'll take that edge off."

Solar only deeply exhales, taking it from his hand and allowing him to light it for her. After exhaling the smoke and watching it dissolve in the air, she shakes her head, "I shouldn't of asked for them in the first place."

Sunwoo looks to her curiously, but was no doubt glad she finally came back down to her senses after listening to her rave about drugs for the last two hours. "Hm, don't say that, it's not like anyone needs to know."

But she only sighs, "you're right. It's just, as nice as it was to let go for all those days and go back to how I used to be, it's not like I can keep this lifestyle," she leans back into the leather booth, "I have to leave tomorrow, go back to my life as an entertainer. If I ever got caught with any of that stuff on me, it'd be over for me, probably a jail sentence."

Blowing a cloud of smoke into the air, he sets his feet on the kitchen table as he takes in what she said, "right, I forgot how harsh it is there," he shrugs, that emotionless tone of his deeper than ever, "well, you went without them for a long time, you'll be fine."

Solar glares at him, "that wasn't exactly the point, Sunwoo. I don't know if I'm ready to go back to living that way."

There's a short silence. "Then stay."

"You know I can't do that."

"You ran away to Korea because you got kicked out, you found a job to make a living there, but now you made up with your family and you have more than a living here," he hums, "so fuck Korea, stay here."

"Sunwoo," she whines, rubbing her temples, "I can't just let everyone down there. I'm in a contract with my agency, I'll get in trouble if I try to just pick up and leave."

He rolls his eyes, "what can I tell you then, Sol?"

She pouts, diverting her eyes to the floor, "I don't know."

Sunwoo had a point.

What did she really want to hear? What was she looking for him to tell her? She wasn't ready to go back, but she didn't have a choice. As much as she loved New York, Korea was calling for her.

She had to go back.


116:00 | the sibling pact

So it was time, whether anyone liked it or not, it was time. It was time for Solar to officially start packing, it was time for her to prepare her mental as if that wasn't all she had been doing (other than drugs and hanging out with Hee and gang members.) It was time for her to go back to her reality, her world of being a global superstar. The world where she was bound to be perfect, where she couldn't make mistakes. It was one that she was fond of, at least she had been. But now that she had a taste of her old life, even with the bitterness of her problems sinking in, she missed it. 

No matter what, though, it was too late for her to turn back. However, that didn't mean she wasn't going to enjoy the last few days in New York. Solar had been forced to stop moping around due to her siblings (who had no idea what was actually going on) and of course, Chanhee and Sunwoo.

It was a late night when it happened. Her nose was shoved deep in her journal, pen angrily scribbling across the page, eyebrows creased in concentration. She was in her zone, as the moonlight left a tint through the curtains, the brief sound of owls hooting somewhere out in the forest behind the house. There's a slight pit pat of rain hitting the roof of the manor, creating a sense of comfort - which she hadn't gotten to feel much after what happened, especially in her own bedroom - and it left a feeling of joy deep down inside of her.

This came as a shock. Ever since she spoke to Junhoe, she hadn't been able to get it off her mind. Her misery had gotten so bad there hadn't been a single thing that could help - not even her best friend had been able to make her feel better. It was why she got so desperate, she turned back to her oldest friend. 

And she felt bad about it. No one knew except for the gang members. She was way too afraid to tell her siblings, not to mention they were completely in the dark about everything else. But even worse, she couldn't gather the courage to tell Hee. There was no telling what he would do, but she could guarantee he would be infuriated. 

In the end, it was her and the gangs little secret. She knew they were good at keeping those, unless they wanted something. 

From having a previous drug addiction, getting back on them was not something that was good for her. Solar never sought out actual treatment for her issue. Her withdrawal had been bad when she got to Korea for that reason. With no way to get them, she had been forced to get over it herself. Actually, she felt like she only had because of Jungkook. That wasn't spoken about enough all because she never really thought about it. Coming to Korea had been a big blurry mess to her by this point, but it was in fact true, he was a big reason she got passed that time in her life. 

Just like Jinhwan helped her with her alcohol addiction years later. But she didn't want to even give him credit for that now.

The want for drugs again now that she had finally had them within her grasp was immense. It was like her entire body was trembling, aching in the craving for them. Her lips were dry, her body shaky, palms sweaty. 

You're better than this, she tries to tell herself, you're finally feeling better, don't go back down the same path.

But she wanted them so bad.

She should've listened when the members warned her.

Like she told herself, though, Solar knew she was stronger than that craving. She had been through this before in many ways, many scenarios. She could get over this just like she did the first time.

Even though all the issues she had on her back didn't help.

"Solar Kim!" her bedroom door slams against the wall as it was so rudely swung open. The skinny legs of Chaerin sashay inside, and there's a rather angry look on her pampered face as she gawks down at her big sister, "why the fuck did Sunwoo just text me telling us to all meet him outside in ten minutes?!"

Solar blinks in complete confusion at her dramatic sister. It didn't take her more than a second to come to the conclusion that there was no possible way anything like that would happen. Why the hell would he do that? Sunwoo was aware her siblings didn't know they still hung out, except for maybe Jaehyun since he didn't dislike Sunwoo. 

But that was before the girl waltzed right before her, where she was comfily perched on her window seat with her journal in her lap, shoving her phone screen in her face. Solar winces from how she nearly got slapped, squinting at the bright screen to see if there was any truth to her words.

Sure enough, there it was.

"Huh, wait," she mutters, trying to understand what was going on in her head. Hurriedly, she picks up her phone beside her, only to see the missed texts she had from the boy. 

Sunu: i have a surprise for you

Sunu: oh, and it includes your siblings being aware of us :)

"Fuck," she grumbles, setting her phone aside and looking back to her angered sister, "all of you got it?"

The girl nods, and Solar sighs. She didn't think it was too big of a deal for Juyeon or Jaehyun, and it wasn't like Yein had a phone to have received anything. Really, Chaerin was the biggest of her worries.

That was only proven when she looks back up to her, only to see her arms crossed over her chest and her green eyes narrowed at her in annoyance. It was clear she was waiting for her big sister to explain, but when Solar is quiet for a bit, she cries in frustration, "are you gonna fucking tell me why this is happening?! Have you been seeing Sunwoo since you got back?! Are you fucking crazy?!"

Before she could even think, there went her sister screaming out idiotic questions. Rolling her eyes, Solar holds up a hand to silence her. Chaerin finally does so, shutting her yapping mouth for once.

"Chill out," she groans, "you didn't even let me say a word."

"Are you cheating on your boyfriend?! You were so good together, and what about Jungkook?! Why would you choose him over either of them?!"

"Chaerin, shut the fuck up!" she snaps in bewilderment at the audacity of her sister. Shaking her head, she motions beside her on the window seat, switching positions so there was enough room for her, "sit, and I'll tell you what's been happening."

"Wow, so you've been keeping a bunch of shit for me, huh?" she snorts, obviously hurt as she falls onto the cushion beside her, "guess our newfound bond meant nothing."

"I did it for your own good," Solar exhales, "I've been trying not to freak anyone out, it'll only make things worse."

"Freak out? I don't freak out over..." she cuts herself off, a guilty look washing over her, "alright, maybe I do."

Chuckling at her sister, the eldest only clears her throat, taking yet another deep breathe, "I haven't been seeing Sunwoo like that, we're just on friendly terms because he's been helping me with a lot. Um, about me and Jinhwan, I recently found out he's been cheating on me from my best friend back in Korea."

She decided to leave out the crucial details about his father, her getting shot by him, and most of all - the dangerous stalker on the loose who bugged her bedroom. It was just better if her sister was unaware of that fact.

Chaerin's mouth falls open in absolute shock. First, she looks sad, almost torn apart. But in a few seconds, her expression forms into pure, livid fury.

"No fucking way, what a piece of shit!" she growls, "and I thought he was fucking nice, I bet he's one big fake motherfucker. He acted like he was so in love with you, then the second you're away from each other he finds someone else! He's fucking lucky if I don't go to Korea myself and beat the fuck out of him!" she ranted on and on, fists clenched in her lap, "I can't believe you didn't tell me this. No wonder you've been with Sunwoo, at least he means it when he says he loves you! I mean, fuck, he's such a dick but it's so clear how he feels about you. He was alone for five years not even knowing where you were all because of his devotion to you!"

The brunette only stares at her sister as she let everything off her chest. It was honestly entertaining to hear, though it was making her think, too.

"God, I'm pissed off, I can only imagine how Sunwoo feels," she shakes her head vigorously, her brown locks falling in her face, "this is the first time in my life I don't mind Sunwoo. No, I definitely mind that fucking short fucker though."

"Chae," Solar sighs, stopping her before she started on another rant again, "calm down, I'm doing better now, not hurting as much. And plus, there is probably more to the story, you know? I shouldn't be making too big of assumptions yet, I have to talk to him first."

"But your best friend told you, there's no reason for him to lie," she cries, "there isn't an excuse for cheating. You better not take him back after what he's done."

Solar scratches the back of her head, thinking back to what happened with her and Sunwoo. She even thought back to her and Jimin. It wasn't like she was innocent in this equation. Though she was torn and upset, though it had apparently been for a while according to Junhoe, it didn't mean she wouldn't give Jinhwan a chance to explain. Their relationship deserved at least that. 

"I'm not," she mutters, "I just want to hear him out, you know?"

"I guess," she rolls her eyes, "but if he tries to tell you some bullshit, you walk out real fast. Jungkook is way better than him, I always thought that."

Somehow that got a chuckle out of her. 

A few moments of silence pass, and Chaerin clears her throat. Scooting a bit closer, she wraps an arm around her big sister's shoulders, "all jokes aside, I'm sorry, sis. I know you really liked him."

She shakes her head, a certain face appearing in her mind, "it's okay, Chae, everything is okay."

The sisters sweet talk was cut off by loud yells. Thank God they weren't actually loud enough to wake their parents, not in a mansion like this. But it still made the girls both look to the culprits in annoyance. 

"Let's fucking go!" Jaehyun is clapping, "who's ready to go on a night trip?!"

Juyeon enters behind him, carrying a Yein in his arms. This raises even more questions as Solar blinks, "sorry - what? A night trip, and why do you have Yein?"

"The text," Jaehyun explains as he walks to fall onto Solar's bed, "Sunwoo so kindly invited us to go have some fun before you leave tomorrow. He told me to bring Yein as apart of a promise you guys made."

She had to think for a second. It didn't take her long to remember her promising Yein that her, Solar, and Sunwoo would all go on a date together. With everything happening, though, she hadn't thought about actually doing it. For that, she felt a little bad, she knew it meant a lot to her baby sister.

"That seems fun, where are we going?!" Chaerin is the first to ask, not minding the thought of being around Sunwoo anymore since the news.

It was confusing to see her react that way to the brothers, but they shrugged it off. "We don't know yet," Jaehyun says, "it's a surprise for Solar."

"I can't wait to see Sunoo!" Yein is screeching in excitement as Juyeon had put her on the ground. She was running around in circles, waving her arms around like a typical kid. On the bright side, it wasn't like an innocent kid like Yein knew what was actually wrong with Sunwoo. And he respected Solar enough to not put any bad things in her head, he tended to just act like a sweet boy who didn't do anything horrible. 

Though she was unsure how that act would work with the other siblings around.

Juyeon had been talking to Chae and Jaehyun about where he thought they would be going. No one seemed to really have much of a clue, especially since Sunwoo wanted them to bring Yein along. It wasn't like they were going to be doing something super dangerous, right? Not with an innocent kid, Sunwoo wasn't that dumb. 

Either way, there were many things making Solar anxious about it. She could only pull her knees to her chest, setting her journal aside and taking deep breathes. Chaerin catches a glance of her sister's state, pursing her lips, "you alright?"

Before she could muster an answer, the smallest of the family had gone up to her biggest sister. Yein blinks up at her with those big, green irises, reaching out to grab her sister's hand so she would get her attention, "sissy, why do you look so sad? Aren't you excited to see Sunoo?"

She couldn't help but chuckle at how precious her baby sister was. Grabbing onto her small hand, she sends her a reassuring, tiny smile, "there's just been a lot going on, but of course I'm excited, Yein."

Chaerin had been staring at her doubtfully as she said those words. It was clear she was lying, and she knew that. There was no way anyone would be okay after finding out what she did. It made Chae so angry that that boy had done such a thing to her sister. Who did he think he was? He was messing with the Lee's, one of the richest, famous families in the state of New York, in the US. As if that wasn't bad enough, she was also connected to the most dangerous family in the states, the Kim's. 

He should've thought twice before he did her like that. He better pray he never ran into any of them.

"What's up with you, though?" Jaehyun pipes into the conversation, narrowing his eyes at her. He knew her better than a lot of people if not better than even Chanhee. How would he not? They were less than a year apart, the first two born children of the family. From day one, they were tied at the hip, an inseparable bond between brother and sister. Jaehyun was protective of Solar for that reason (and all of his sisters,) and he could read her like a book when he needed to. "I can see through that look on your face."

"Yeah, you've been weird," Juyeon adds, "we all have known it, I was just too scared to ask ever since you got hurt in that 'accident'."

She grew pale at the mention. That was definitely not something she wanted to bring up to them. It would be a very bad idea being that they were about to see the very person involved in that whole fiasco.

"Uh," she stutters, "it's just - guy problems."

Her voice was so low she wasn't sure if they heard her. Chaerin glares at her impatiently, not getting why she didn't just tell them. When Solar has yet to explain further, she heaves out a deep breathe, "Sol, you should tell them, they should know about that piece of shit. Do you want me to? I will if you don't."

While she loved her sister, sometimes she wanted to punch her. This was one of those times.

"Chae," she holds a hand to her head, sighing, but her sister's stubborn expression didn't change. She realized that her brothers would find out eventually anyway thanks to Chaerin's big mouth, so with a dull exhale, she shrugs, "fine, whatever."

"So, that Jinhwan guy she was dating cheated on her when he went back to Korea," she begins, tone full of anger, "can you believe that? He was only away from her for what - like a month or so - and he just can't keep his dick in his pants! Such a fucking prick, I always preferred that Jungkook guy. I mean, he wrote a song for her and everything about how he trusted her decision and would always look over her. Where the hell is this Jinhwan guy's compassion?!"

From the fact her sister could never help herself from overdoing it and going way too far into her thoughts, Solar buries her face in her hands. Not even to mention the fact she blatantly tended to curse in front of Yein, but at this point it was too late to assert that. Nothing in the world could stop Chaerin Lee's mouth.

"Wow, are you fucking kidding me?" Jaehyun gawks, his fists clenching at his sides. She knew he would react the worst to this out of all of them because of how protective he was. "I can't fucking - holy shit, this guy has some nerve. He got you into all that shit that happened back on that first day in New York, and for what?"

"All what shit?" Juyeon asks.

Solar gives her older brother a warning glance. "Long story," is all he says with a groan, "I'm coming back to Korea with you, no way you're handling this on your own. That guy deserves a piece of my mind."

This was not what she wanted right now.

"Jae," she breathes, "that's nonsense, I'm going to handle it."

"Bullshit," he snaps, "I'll tell you who'll handle it, and it'll be me."

"Jae," she tries again sternly, but he only scoffs in disbelief.

"I'm not letting someone treat you like that," he insists harshly, arms crossed over his chest.

"He's got a point," Chae chimes in just as Solar was about to disagree once again, "remember our pact? We don't let people hurt each other, we weren't raised that way."

Chaerin had a point. The once two, then three, four, and now five siblings had always been close. Before Solar left, they did everything together when she wasn't with Hee or Sunwoo. Since they were all kids, they were best friends just as they were siblings. And they swore to never let each other get hurt or wronged. They were raised that way, to love each other, to be there when no one else was. 

And after what happened and how much the Lee siblings regretted what they did to Solar, they'd never make the same mistake again. 

"They're right, Sol," Juyeon nervously speaks up. He was still a little anxious around his big sister even though they made up, that guilt would always be a part of him. "But maybe we should talk about this tomorrow."

"Yeah, speaking of," Chae mumbles, and only then did they notice she had Solar's phone in her hand, "think this is our queue, Sunwoo texted," her eyes squint at another notification, "and so did Chim, he sent a photo - ooh, is that Jungkook?!"

"Huh?" Sol screeches, snatching the phone out of her hand. She sighs as she looks down at the picture Jimin sent her, he seemed to be sending photos of Jungkook more often now. It was almost like he knew something happened.

He guess he might of guessed since she randomly asked him to pick her up at the airport instead of her 'boyfriend.'

Either way, she was happy to see him. Jungkook was always a sight that made her heart clench. But right then, it seemed to ache more in her chest than ever. 

"Let's go," she finally sighs, turning off the phone and shoving it in her pocket, "let's hope we don't get caught by our parents this time."



117:00 | breaking and entering in style

Sunwoo's Bugatti was shimmering under the street lights. It was probably one of the most expensive cars in the world, and it was no shock he had one. The siblings had yet to see it, and they make sounds of ooh as they walk onto the porch towards the car. 

The boy in the drivers seat had rolled the window down, bright smile on his face as soon as his eyes landed on a certain girl. 

"Nice ride~," Jaehyun hums, opening the backseat and sliding inside.

There's a rap song Solar didn't know blasting from the radio, and Yein had been bouncing around in excitement. Unable to contain herself, she leans forward and climbs onto the middle compartment. Her green eyes shine as she looks to the boy driving, who was casually smoking a cigarette, enjoying the music playing, and beams, "Sunoo, I missed you!"

Taking the cigarette out of his mouth, he blows the smoke out in a different direction before looking to Yein. The hard, violent crime boss everyone knew so well vanished in that moment. "Sol is so smart, Sunoo, she helped me get good grades!" she was crying, "did you make good grades like sissy, too?"

From how well everyone knew the answer to that, the siblings start snickering.

Not really getting what he meant by that - as in he made horrible grades due to never being at school - Yein only shrugs and nods as if she understood. "No, you're one of the smartest people I know," her brother responds casually, "maybe if you would've actually attended the classes."

They went on to make jokes and laugh about old memories they had. Chaerin and Juyeon joined in, talking about the parties they used to go to and all the drugs they used to do. Solar wasn't much for the talk, since it was a weird time in her life she didn't feel like thinking about with what happened recently. If she had drugs on her mind, the cravings would start again, and she was trying hard to avoid those.

So instead, she hums along to the music playing on the radio. Sunwoo had changed the channel to songs she actually knew, as they were just old pop songs they used to listen to when they were younger. The sense of nostalgia only grew within her veins, but she let it stay.

The glass of the window is cold against her cheek as she leans against it. Whatever road they were on seemed to never end, and she found herself wondering where the hell they were even going. But when she asked Sunwoo not long ago, he shook his head with a chuckle, you'll see, princess.

She wanted to hit him sometimes, but she had to accept that whatever he was doing, he was doing it for her. So it must be something she'll love.

With that, she was left in anticipation. 

"No, no, no - wait!" Chaerin is giggling, "you guys remember when the cops showed up at our party, and Sunwoo went up and just said 'you should leave' and told them who his father was and they fucking bolted. Like come on, who had that sort of freedom as teenagers? Ugh, the good old days."

"Seriously, they didn't want to mess with you," Juyeon nods in agreement.

Sunwoo shrugs, one hand driving and the other holding another cigarette, "perks of having a psychotic father with power everywhere."

There was a certain sadness in the back of his eyes, you could only see it if you concentrated hard enough on those brown irises. He hid it well, but every now and then, you could see it; you could see that as stubborn and hard-headed as he was, it hurt a part of him. His father's doings, the trauma it left him with, it left a mark on him.

Solar couldn't help but peer at him sadly. She always felt for Sunwoo in that regard. He was born into a fucked up family, one where he had no mother so he was left with his arrogant, evil father who only used him to better his company and kill his foes. He didn't ask to be turned into the monster he was, and he wasn't one in reality, it was forced upon him. Though he pulled the trigger, the gun was forced into his hands, and it meant death for him if he didn't do it.

He catches her glance only to send her a smile, the car swerving onto a different street, before he announces, "we're here."

Everyone sits up eagerly like children awaiting their dessert. No one knew what to expect, their eyes were wide with curiosity. Yein was woken up from the commotion of their movement, rubbing her eyes as she sits up straight to see what was going on. 

"No fucking way," Chaerin mumbles in disbelief, eyes raking over the scenery that was before them, right outside their window.

"Kim Sunwoo," Solar gawks, green eyes twinkling with joy as she turns to him, "first of all, I'm impressed, and second of all - are you crazy?"

Turning off the car, he chuckles at her as he opens his door, "Should I even answer that, Solar Lee?"

Shaking her head, he had a point, "probably not."

"Where are we?" Yein is asking, wondering why everyone was reacting the way they were. She finally was met with the bright lights as Chaerin opened the door and they all climbed out, to which resulted in her screaming in cheer, "whoa, no way, Sunoo is the best surprise-r ever!"

Everyone laughs at her words. 

Standing before the park, the lights were nearly blinding. That was with most of them off since it was in fact closed.

"So what the hell is your plan?" Chaerin raises a brow in question as they're walking up the front entrance seconds later. 

Before he could reply, Jaehyun does for him, "break in, cut off the cameras, turn on the power, and have fun, I'm guessing."

His sister wasn't impressed, "thanks, smart ass."

Already picking the lock at the front gate, Sunwoo hums, "well, he's right." Suddenly, he realizes something, and pulls something out of his pocket. Already knowing what to do, Solar covers Yein's eyes and ears as he pulls the trigger on something. "Didn't want the alarm going off," he informs everyone, "should be fine now."

With that, he gets back to work, and before you knew it, the gates to the amusement park were wide open. Not really understanding what they were doing, it was a normal day for Yein. Arms in the air, she runs into the park with bright cries leaving her mouth.

The others follow close behind, not wanting to lose her in the massive place. She stops in the middle of the walkway, looking around in confusion, "but why is it so dark?"

"We haven't turned the power on yet, Yein," Solar tells her, patting her back. The girl nods as she takes in the information.

"I can go do that," Jaehyun offers, "isn't my first rodeo."

Chaerin peers at him blankly, "when the hell did you break into an amusement park previously?"

He only shrugs, "I've done a lot of things."

Before anyone could ask, he went off somewhere to get the power up and running.

"Well," Sunwoo smiles as he walks to the brunettes side, "what shall we do first?"

She could only shake her head in dismay at him, laughing lightly as she gently hits his chest, "you're something else, Kim Sunwoo."

Sending her a wink, he only responds, "tell me something I don't know, sweetheart," before looking to the little girl before them, "come on, Yein, let's go pick what ride to go on first."

"Okay!" she excitedly agrees, taking the hand Sunwoo offers to her.

Yein was in the middle of talking about how long it had been since she got to go to an amusement park since her parents were so busy and didn't have time anymore. Sunwoo had glanced behind him to see where Solar was. His eyes land on her, and he walks a little slower to reach out and grab her hand with the one that was free.

There's a slight breeze blowing, but the brief rain that there'd been earlier was gone. All that was left was the cold air.

"I'm not a kid!" the girl immediately retorts with a pout.

Jaehyun returned to the group after turning on the power. "So what's first?"

Jaehyun shrugs, "I'm sure it'll be fine if you just strap her in correctly."

"It will be," Sunwoo pipes in, "don't worry yourself," he tells Solar, squeezing her hand that he was holding.

It wasn't that she didn't trust her siblings to keep their littlest safe. Surely it wasn't very hard to work the safety compartments of a rollercoaster. There was something else bothering her, something that was itching at her skin, bruising her sanity.

How the hell would he feel if he ended up doing it to her again? The short answer - a piece of shit. He just didn't think much about it, he figured she could handle them, that she was smart enough now.

With how much the girl preached about taking care of herself, he tried to let her do that.

Hoping no one noticed, she clears her throat and lets Sunwoo drag her along the concrete paths of the amusement park. The other siblings follow them casually, laughing as if there wasn't a single thing wrong in their lives.

It was nice to have that sort of quality time with them. It meant a lot to her that Sunwoo included all of her siblings in this. He meant it when he said he wanted to give her a memorable last night in New York.

Confused because her big sister wasn't usually so overly strict and nervous, she turns to her as she goes, trying to reassure her with her tiny voice, "I'm okay, sissy."

Squeezing her eyes shut, Solar tried to calm herself down. It wasn't that she was actually freaking about Yein falling, it was that damn craving.

Chunking another one of his cigarettes to the ground, Jaehyun shrugs, "I can probably figure it out."

But the eldest brother rolls his eyes, hitting his sister's back as he hums, "don't worry, lil' sis, you'll be fine."

"Ow!" the dramatic girl snapped as soon as his hand even grazed her back, "fuck you."

"Come on, guys, let's go!" Juyeon was crying, already going up the steps himself, "Solar and Yein are already at the top!"

They were indeed. Solar was bouncing up and down from her toes to her heel, her brain thinking hard about the one thing that had been torturing her. She had been okay for a while. It seemed that craving only came back to haunt her whenever she got anxious, angry, or sad. Any strong emotion that flew through her body made her want them - bad.

Looking at Yein, the little girl was too busy looking around at how the ride was. She kept clapping in excitement, boasting about how she felt like a big kid now.

Positive she wasn't paying attention, the brunette pulls a certain something out of her pocket. Screwing off the cap while keeping it hidden by her side, she hurriedly takes one out. Without a second thought, she nearly choked from shoving it in her mouth and swallowing it so quickly.

As soon as she felt the pill go down, she seemed to breathe again. Closing her eyes, she felt her nerves return to a normal state.

Exhaling, she walks up to Yein, who was trying to climb into the ride, "hold up, Yein, they're almost up here. Jaehyun or Sunwoo are gonna have to figure out how to work it."

The girl frowns, but nods anyway. Backing away, she returns back to her sister's side. Her small hand reached out, grabbing her big sisters. It wouldn't of caught Solar off guard if she hadn't been in her own mental world.

When she looks down at the little girl, her eyes were shimmering under the light. "Do you wanna sit with me, sissy?"

"Yeah," he hums, "yeah, I think so."

"Three."

And like that, she ran, she ran to the sound of gunshots.

And she was dreading it.

"You've still got problems here you haven't solved," he convicts with a light laugh, "you're not getting it, little sister."

She blinks at him, a blank expression evident across her face. "No," she remarks, "I have no fucking idea."

Her brother laughs for real this time. It takes him a minute to calm down as the bright sound pours from his lips, and he shakes his head in awe as he returns back to normal. Running a hand through his hair, he sighs as he explains sternly, "you're telling me while you haven't gotten cozy with Sunwoo since you got here?"

"Huh?" she gawks, "are you implying I cheated on my boyfriend?"

"In a feasible sense, yes."

"Jae, shut the fuck up," she groans, she would never admit he wasn't wrong, "there's nothing going on with Sunwoo and I, we're just us. It's not like we're together."

But his face was full of the fact he didn't believe a single word coming out of her mouth.

"Sissy!" a screaming Yein was heard, tumbling down the stairs in her own manner. Just the sight of her sweet baby sister made her smile, "sissy, I came to cheer you up before you have to leave!"

Juyeon had come down shortly after Yein, joining them on the sofas. It was unknown to anyone where Chaerin was, but it was most likely locked up in her room.

"Aw, Yein," she gushes as her sister climbs to sit neck and neck with her, "you don't have to cheer me up."

"Yeah I do," she shakes her head, "I'm super sad that you're leaving, so I know you must be super duper sad."

She could only giggle at the innocence, wrapping an arm around her little sister and pulling her into a tight embrace. "It'll be okay, Yein, you can call me whenever you want."

Her little sister was more than happy to hear that. It wasn't long until she went on to boast about how she couldn't wait to see her big sister on TV, listen to her music, and tell everyone at school how she had the coolest sister in the world. Hearing something like that took a lot of the stress of Solar's shoulders. Her little sister was part of the reason she did what she did, and she loved her to death for it.

Minutes later, a door had opened and closed upstairs. Chaerin's hair is tied in a ponytail atop her head, a hoodie many sizes too big for her hanging loosely off her body. All she had been doing was sitting in bed all day on her phone, trying to resist the urge eating her alive and comprehend the fact her big sister had been on drugs again. There was no telling how Solar was feeling, with the fact Chae had stolen her drugs, without them. 

The two sisters hadn't spoken much last night. As soon as they got in the car, it had been a mass of confusion and fear. Sunwoo was sped off down the road as fast as his Bugatti could drive, and only on the way home did the siblings start to ask questions.


"Does anyone want to explain why we just got shot at?" Juyeon asks, surprisingly calm despite the events that took place.

"Well," Sunwoo hums, "a lot of people do hate us."

His sarcasm wasn't helpful to anyone. Chae was still shaken up, her body trembling as she rubs her forearms, this was all too much at once. First, she found drugs on her sister and then they got shot at? What the fuck kind of night was this?

"Just fucking explain!" she snaps at the boy in the driver's seat, before turning to her sister, "and you explain! I know you two are fucking in on whatever the fuck is happening and I'm not in the fucking mood to be in the dark!"

Solar swallows a lump in her throat, not really wanting to mess with her sister. She was the only one out of her siblings who knew about the drugs, and the last thing she wanted was for her to out her doings. It wasn't like she was proud of it. 

"Uh," she clears her throat, but no words came out after that.

Sunwoo glances at her from where he was speeding down the road. Through the mirror, he raises a brow at her, mouthing is it okay as in if she wanted him to explain. The brunette nods to him, sending him a small smile before she diverts their eye contact.

Gripping the steering wheel, he deadpans, "someone from Korea is after Solar, they want to ruin her career and her life."

There's a long silence in the car. The only sound you could hear was the engine roaring and the tires scraping against the road.

It was when Chaerin breaks the quiet, "so you're saying someone wants to fucking kill her?! Oh, great!"

"I'm unsure of their intent," Sunwoo responds in that monotone voice of his, "I assume they wanted one of you dead, not her. They wanted to send a message."

"Holy fucking shit," Juyeon mutters.

The only one able to piece everything together was Jaehyun, since he was there that night. The rest of the siblings were just going to have to be left in the dark, it was all they needed to know. And just that bit of information was putting them in enough danger.


After everyone knew about someone being after Sol, her and Chaerin never spoke of the drugs again. They seemed to have bigger issues, bigger things on their minds. She was hoping they never would have to speak of it again.

"I'm here," a sigh is heard from the bottom of the stairwell, the petite girl entering the room and falling onto the sofa, "I didn't want to miss my goodbye."

Chaerin sends a smile towards her big sister. It was one that was meant to tell her everything was okay. She forgave her for what she did, in the end it wasn't like she had a right to be mad. Solar was going through a lot, and she understood that after last night. Sometimes drugs felt like all you had, she knew that much.

"Don't you have to leave at 6?" Jaehyun asks, eyes staring at the clock, "we're getting scary close."

"Yeah," she nods, seeing if he was right. Sure enough, the clock was striking 5.

"I don't see why you're letting Sunwoo take you to the airport instead of us," Chaerin grumbles, "I mean, I get it, he's your bodyguard or whatever. But what are you gonna do when you're back there? It's not like you have your own Sunwoo in Korea - you know, unless you're getting back with Jungkook."

"Chae," she sighs, shaking her head in disbelief at her sister, "I've got it under control, and it's just easiest if Sunwoo takes me."

Her younger sister just stares at her with a look that said fucking liar. But there wasn't anything she could say to change her mind. In reality, she had nothing under control. Solar was the definition of a mess, but she was not about to admit it to any of her siblings.

"Solar, dear!" a cry was heard from the double doors of the manor as they swung open. Her mother had practically pushed over the maids who opened the door for her, her high heels clicking against the tiled floor as she ran into the living room, "my sweet daughter, I can't believe you're leaving already."

The siblings winced as they watched their mother baby the oldest sister. Solar couldn't help but accept her embrace either way, knowing her mother would be hugging her every five minutes until she left.

"Are you feeling okay?" she asks as she pulls away, placing the back of her hand on the girl's head, "No sickness, nausea? It's very bad to get on a plane if you're not feeling well. Have you ate?"

"Mother," Solar breathes, smiling to reassure her worry, "I'm perfectly fine, okay?"

"Right," she nods, pursing her lips as she turns to search for one of the maids, "get us some snacks, please - oh, and me a glass of wine."

"Wine, mother, really?" Chaerin is unimpressed as she looks to her dramatic mother, and everyone wondered where she got it from.

Her mother doesn't even glance at the girl as she sits on one of the couches, "What? I need to destress, how do I think straight when my child is going back across the world?"

The siblings all groan, mentally exhausted from how much their mother clung to her oldest daughter. As if it hadn't been back enough when they were younger, it was to another extent now.

"Your father should be here soon," she was saying as the maids brought in what she requested. Taking a sip of the wine, she clears her throat, "when are you leaving?"

Realizing she had no idea what the answer to that question was, she hurriedly looks to the clock.

Oh, shit.

As if on queue, her phone vibrates in her back pocket. "Um," she pauses, taking it out and squinting down at the screen.

Sunu: I'm here, are you ready?

With one deep breathe, she looked up to her family as she deadpans, "now."


121:00 | the saddest goodbye

The family goodbye went exactly how one would have expected. A ton of tears were shed, a lot of begging for her to not go, and a lot of you better call us often's were said. Her siblings hugged her to death, whispering in her ear lowly for her parents not to hear about how she better keep them updated on everything and stay fucking safe. They were kind enough to keep who was driving covered, loading her bags in the backseat for her so her parents didn't see it was Sunwoo. They most likely assumed it was Hee, whom she still had to go say goodbye to at the time.

"I love you, sissy!" Yein had hugged her legs, "I'll miss you everyday, please come back soon!"

"I will, Yein," the brunette giggles as she kneels down on the ground to hug her youngest sister, "I promise, okay?"

Holding out her pinky finger to the girl, it causes a smile to spread over her face. Without a second thought, she grabs her pinky, squeezing it with her own, "now you have to, you pinky promised!"

"Don't worry, Yein," was the last thing she said to her little sister.

"I love you guys, I'll be home before you know it!" were the last words she yelled to her family out the window, making sure they couldn't see Sunwoo. 

Her mother had hugged her father in tears, waving goodbye to her beloved daughter she cherished so much. Solar knew it hurt her family to see her go, but she knew that they knew she didn't have a choice. She was an adult now, an adult who had grown out of the way of life at the Castle. She grew out of the way that you were supposed to live at home, go to medical school, until eventually you could live in your own manor in the Castle. That was how it went, and it had never changed.

Not until now.

Chanhee had nearly beat her up when he saw her. Her best friend made her swear she wouldn't forget he was number one, and that she should save a room in her apartment because he would be living with her in the near future. Solar had laughed at it, but she had a feeling he probably wasn't joking.

The rest of her best friends, and even Hee in the end, had shed more tears than she expected. They weren't usually criers, but it just was weird to see Solar leave again. How could it not strike a soft spot in your heart?

Lastly, Sunwoo stopped by the Kim residence so she could say goodbye to the members. They were a bit more ecstatic than the rest, being a mix of high and drunk so they didn't really seem to comprehend emotion as well. Hyunjoon had squeezed the life out of her, crying about how he loved her and her beautiful face to death. Eric made the same idiotic jokes, and Sangyeon warned her about always being aware of her surroundings. 

Some of them even offered her drugs for the ride, but she and Sunwoo politely declined. She was still working on forgetting about that downfall, even if the craving was eating her alive at points. The last thing she needed was to give into it.

It was when they'd headed out that the energy died down. The car was quiet, other than the sound of the indie music playing in the background from the speakers. Sunwoo was in deep thought, deep thought about if he actually had the guts to allow the girl he loved go on a plane across the world. He knew that person was still after her, he knew they weren't a joke, they weren't afraid even when he was by her side. Who knew what they would do when she was all alone, like a puppy in the wild? He wouldn't be able to protect her.

Solar had leaned her head against the cold window, watching the scenery of New York as they passed it. The Upper East Side, her beloved home that had brought her so many good and bad memories. The life of privilege she grew up in was also a life of pressure and isolation. Even then, she still missed it sometimes.

She didn't have a choice. There was no going back to the girl she once was, the life she once lived. The happiness she once felt then was long gone.

"How are you feeling?" Sunwoo had asked, breaking into her thoughts. His brown irises peer over at her for only a split second before he focuses on the road again.

The brunette doesn't look at him. Instead, her eyes stay fixated on the outside world, a sigh leaving her lips, "I don't really know, anxious, stressed, worried," she began to list out adjectives that described her emotions.

The gang leader purses his lips. He's in deep thought for a second, before he blurts, "the cravings have been bad, haven't they?"

She wasn't surprised he knew this. Anyone could tell she had been a little more jumpy than usual.

"Yup," she says without a thought, "I can get through it, I have before, but I don't know about Chae."

His face falls as he hears her words. "Wait," he pauses in awe, "Chaerin's the one who caught you and took them?"

She only nods in response, burying her face in her hands as she recalls it, "I know, it's bad, really bad. I need you to promise you'll deal with that, she can't get on drugs again."

Sunwoo exhales deeply, probably not thrilled about having to add that to his to-do list, but yet agrees, "alright, I will."

"Thanks, Sunwoo, for everything."

Solar had to wear a disguise to go into the airport. Her staff and manager had offered a million times to send security to escort her so it would be safer, but she declined politely. The last thing she wanted was to bring attention to herself and Sunwoo. They both knew he was not about to let her check out through the airport alone.

So there they went, shoes clicking against the tiled floor of the airport. Solar had a mask over her face and a bucket hat on, covering the majority so hopefully no one recognized her. Keeping her head low, she and Sunwoo make their way to the waiting area for her plane.

"I hate this," Sunwoo deadpans as they take a seat on one of the many black rows of chairs. He crosses one leg over the other, looking anxious for the first time in his life as he taps his foot against the floor.

Solar curiously looks to him, raising a brow, "it'll be okay, don't look so freaked out, you're scaring me."

She was really trying to reassure him. Solar herself was more afraid than anything. Hell, now that she knew this person wasn't afraid to shoot at her and even somehow managed to break into the Castle, what else could they do? Her thoughts were as nervous as Sunwoo's, but yet worse. She was a mess, a catastrophe waiting to happen. For the first time in a long time, she had no idea how she was going to live without Sunwoo by her side.

And Jinhwan, she grimaced, rubbing her temples, she had to face Jinhwan.

"Fuck, I'm just so mad I can't go with you," Sunwoo groans, pulling at his hair, "this person is no joke, I thought for sure we would catch them when they showed up, but they never came back again - they're smart, Sol."

"Sunwoo," she breathes, "there's nothing you can do, I have to go back."

"Just - keep me updated," he sighs, "if anything happens, I can catch a plane there, alright?"

She sends him a small smile, nodding, "yeah, yeah, I will."

The brunette tried to steady her breathing as she rose to her feet. Throwing the bags she would be taking on the plane over her shoulder, she turns to Sunwoo one last time. 

A crowd had formed in their area, and many people were hurriedly rushing onto the plane. She tries to keep her head down for this reason, sending him a small worried smile, "well, guess it's time."

The boy stares at her for a long while. His eyes rake over her entire body, as if he was trying to memorize every single aspect of her before she left. When they're back at her eyes, there's that same twinkle in his brown irises, and he steps forward to pull her into a tight hug.

Caught off guard for a moment, it didn't take long for comfort to spread through her veins. Burying her face in his chest, she inhaled that scent of smoke and cologne, the one she used to love so much. 

She couldn't lie, she'd grown to love it again.

His breathe fanned her neck, the hot sensation sending chills through her body. The girl laughs nervously, shaking her head as she hits his chest, "Sunwoo, calm down with that weird thing you do, okay?" he only winks at her, and she rolls her eyes, "but thank you," she admits anyway, "really."

"No need, sweetheart," he hums, "you've thanked me enough."

She was upset that she knew what he meant.

"Not the time!" she snaps, scoffing in disbelief, "you're an idiot."

"I'm not the idiot, your little boyfriend is the idiot," he retorts, "which is why if this isn't some sort of misunderstanding I am going to fly there and personally slaughter him myself."

Though this was a commonly used expression - Sunwoo wasn't kidding.

"That won't be necessary," she sighs, "no matter what happens."

He shakes his head, pulling her into another hug. This time, when he pulls away he leaves a lingering kiss on her forehead, "just stay safe, Sol, okay?"

"I will, Sunu."

"Flight 104 leaving in one minute," the intercom chimes.

"Well, you better go, princess," he breathes, a certain sadness evident in his voice. His fingers run across her cheek, the soft touch enough to make her shiver.

Adjusting the bag on her shoulder, she takes his hand off her cheek, holding it with her own for a minute. "Yup, I'm going," she nods, taking a few steps back, but yet her hand was still in his. Solar sends the boy a smile as she finally lets it fall, "bye, Sunwoo."

"Bye, princess," he returns her smile, but for the first time, you could see the emotion his was full of. His hands fall back to his side, fingers tingling from her lasting touch as he fiddles with the hem of his leather jacket. He was already itching, itching for her to come back, itching for her to turn around and change her mind. It was an itch something like drugs or cigarettes couldn't fix. 

Only she could.

He watched her go all the way to the plane boarding area. Just seeing her in the distance made his heart flutter. Sunwoo was a mess when it came to this girl, an indescribable, idiotic mess.

There was nothing he could do to make her stay. And worst of all, there was nothing he could do to keep her safe while she was all the way across the world. Yet, he wanted to do what he could. This is why he keeps his glance on her, making sure there wasn't anyone suspicious peering at her from the side. A place like the airport wouldn't be a bad place to stage something. 

But there was nothing. Sunwoo was smart enough at this to catch even the slightest of things, but he saw no sign of odd activity that would put her in danger. 

Watching as she boards the plane, turning around one last time to wave at him with that grin on her face, a breathe of relief leaves his lips. I love you, he was thinking like the lovestruck kid he was at heart, before shaking the childish thought away as he disappears into the plane. 

She'll be okay, he tells himself, when suddenly his phone dings in his back pocket.
